The Obligation of Seeking Essential Knowledge (al-Qadr al-Daruri)
Definition-ruling commentary on the hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'al-qadr al-daruri' and state why seeking it is fard 'ayn on every Muslim.

Core Idea
Seeking essential religious knowledge is fard 'ayn; the hadith is limited to the necessary amount.

This passage clarifies a widely cited hadith on seeking knowledge. While its wording seems general, the Hanafi commentator restricts its scope to what is indispensable for every Muslim's faith and practice. Understanding this limitation is crucial for knowing one's minimum religious duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its textual basis
The hadith 'طلب العلم فريضة على كل مسلم ومسلمة' is cited. Note that its chain is hasan according to some scholars, so it is a valid proof.
The hadith is marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) and recorded by multiple compilers.
2
Locate the definition of 'ilm
The commentator explicitly states: 'والمراد بالعلم في هذا الحديث هو القدر الضروري' – what is meant by knowledge in this hadith is the necessary amount.
This restriction is key: not all knowledge, only what is personally essential.
3
Understand the legal implication
Since the hadith uses the word 'فريضة' (obligation), and it is limited to essential knowledge, seeking that amount is fard 'ayn on every responsible Muslim.
Fard 'ayn means individually obligatory; neglecting it is sinful.
4
Distinguish from other types of knowledge
Advanced or optional knowledge (e.g., detailed fiqh, Arabic grammar, tafsir) is not covered by this obligation; it may be fard kifayah or recommended.
The definition prevents overburdening the average Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن طلب العلم فريضة على كل مسلم ومسلمة»، وبالتقصير لا تعذر. [١] قوله : طلب العلم ؛ هذا لفظ الحديث المرفوع أخرجه ابن ماجة والبيهقي والبَزَّارُ وابنُ عبد البر في كتاب العلم وتمـام (۲) في «فوائده» وغيرهم، وأكثر طرقه معلولة وصحح بعض الأئمة بعض طرقه. وقال المزي(٣) : إن طرقه تبلغ به رتبة الحَسَن، وحسنه ابن القطان صاحب ابن ماجة أيضاً، وقد بسط الكلام فيه الزين العراقي (4) في تخريج أحاديث إحياء العلوم» (٤) وغيره، والمراد بالعلم في هذا الحديث : هو القدر الضروري.
For seeking knowledge is an obligation upon every Muslim, male and female, and through negligence it is not excused. [1] His saying: 'Seeking knowledge'; this is the wording of the marfu' hadith recorded by Ibn Majah, al-Bayhaqi, al-Bazzar, and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr in the Book of Knowledge, and Tammam (2) in his Fawa'id and others, and most of its chains are defective, but some imams authenticated some of its chains. Al-Mizzi (3) said: Its chains reach the rank of hasan, and Ibn al-Qattan, the companion of Ibn Majah, also deemed it hasan. Al-Zayn al-'Iraqi (4) discussed it at length in his Takhrij Ahadith Ihya' al-'Ulum and elsewhere. And what is meant by 'knowledge' in this hadith is the necessary amount (al-qadr al-daruri).
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling commentary on the phrase 'طلب العلم فريضة' from the matn. The commentator first cites the hadith 'طلب العلم فريضة على كل مسلم ومسلمة' and then discusses its chain of transmission. He notes that although most chains are defective (ma'lula), some imams have authenticated some chains. Al-Mizzi and Ibn al-Qattan considered it hasan. The commentator then defines what is meant by 'العلم' in this hadith: it is the necessary amount (القدر الضروري) of religious knowledge — i.e., what every responsible Muslim must know of the basics of faith and practice. This limits the general command to the essential duties, excluding advanced or optional knowledge.

Key Terms
القدر الضروري (al-qadr al-daruri): The minimum amount of religious knowledge necessary for a Muslim to fulfill his or her basic duties, such as knowledge of iman, prayer, fasting, and halal/haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what kind of knowledge is meant by 'العلم' in the hadith 'طلب العلم فريضة على كل مسلم ومسلمة'?
A) All knowledge, religious and secular
B) The necessary amount (القدر الضروري) of religious knowledge
C) Only knowledge of the Quran
D) Knowledge of fiqh only

Key Takeaway
The obligation to seek knowledge (fard 'ayn) is limited to the essential amount needed for every Muslim's basic religious duties.

Milk of a Man and Enema Do Not Establish Foster Relationship
Stating that milk from a man and enema do not establish foster relationship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two cases where milk entering the body does not create foster relationship prohibition and apply the Hanafi principle of radāʿ.

Core Idea
Only real milk drunk by mouth establishes radāʿ; man's milk and enema do not count.

This passage addresses common misconceptions about foster relationships in Hanafi fiqh. It clarifies that not all milk-like substances or all methods of ingestion create the prohibition of marriage. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly applying the laws of radāʿ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognise that drinking milk from a man and receiving an enema of breast milk are the two acts being ruled upon. The ruling is that neither establishes a foster relationship (radāʿ).
2
Locate the dalil
The text uses analogy (qiyās) and a principle. For man's milk, it compares to fish blood which is not real blood. For enema, it invokes the condition that radāʿ requires drinking (shurb).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy shows that man's milk is not real milk (ḥaqīqī) but a moisture, so it cannot carry the ruling of radāʿ. The principle of drinking excludes mere entry via enema or ear drops.
4
Note the distinction with dead woman's milk
The text contrasts with milk from a dead woman, which does establish prohibition because it is real milk, regardless of how ingested. This highlights that the key is the substance, not the source's life status.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school firmly holds that only real human milk drunk by mouth within the radāʿ period creates a foster relationship. This position is from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and is muftā bihī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما في لبن رجل، واحتقان صبي بلبنها. (كما في لبن رجل) : أي إذا نَزَلَ للرَّجل لبن فشربَهُ صبي لا يتعلق به حرمة الرضاع، (واحتقان صبي بلبنها. [1] قوله : لا يتعلّق به ؛ لأنّ لبنه ليس بلبن حقيقة ، بل هو رطوبة شبيهة به ، كدم السمك ليس بدم حقيقة، فلا يتعلق به حكم من أحكام الرضاعة، بخلاف لبن المرأة الميتة، فإنّه يتعلق به التحريم، سواءً مصه من ثديها بعد موتها، أو حلبه فشربه ؛ لكونه مما تتعلق به الحرمة. [٢] قوله : واحتقان ؛ عطفٌ على لبن ،رجل، والمناسب أن يقال : حقن، فإنّه يقال : حقنتُ المريض إذا أوصلتُ الدواء إلى باطنه من دبر بالمحقنة، واحتقن هو لازم، والاسم الحقنة – بالضم – . ومن المعلوم أن الصبي لا يحتقن بنفسه، بل يحقنه غيره، والحاصل أن أحكام الرضاعة إنّما تثبت بشرب اللبن لا بمجرد وصوله إلى باطنه، فلا يتعلق التحريم بإيصاله إلى جوف صبي في مدة الرضاع بالمحقنة ، وكذا بإقطارِهِ في أذنه أو إحليله وغير ذلك.
Like the milk of a man, and the enema of a child with her milk. (Like the milk of a man): meaning, if milk descends for a man and a child drinks it, no prohibition of radāʿ attaches. (And the enema of a child with her milk). [1] He said: it does not attach because his milk is not milk in reality, but is a moisture resembling it, like the blood of fish is not blood in reality, so no ruling of radāʿ attaches, unlike the milk of a dead woman, for prohibition attaches, whether he sucks it from her breast after her death or milks it and drinks it, because it is something to which prohibition attaches. [2] He said: 'and enema' is conjoined to 'milk of a man', and it would be more appropriate to say 'ḥuqin' (he was given an enema), for it is said 'ḥaqantul-marīḍa' when you deliver medicine into his interior from the anus via an enema, and 'iḥtaqana' is the intransitive, and the noun is 'ḥuqna' (with ḍamma). And it is known that the child does not give himself an enema, rather someone else does. The conclusion is that the rulings of radāʿ are only established by drinking milk, not by mere arrival into his interior, so no prohibition attaches to delivering it into the belly of a child during the period of radāʿ via an enema, and likewise dropping it into his ear or his urethra and other things.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It clarifies two exceptions to the general principle that radāʿ (foster relationship) is established by milk entering the child's stomach. First, milk from a man does not create prohibition because it is not real milk but a moisture similar to it, analogous to fish blood which is not real blood. This is proven by analogy (qiyās). However, milk from a dead woman does create prohibition because it is true milk, regardless of how it is ingested. Second, an enema (iḥtiqān) with milk does not create prohibition because the rulings of radāʿ depend on drinking (shurb), not mere entry into the body. The commentary expands on the linguistic usage and confirms that other methods like drops in the ear or urethra also do not establish radāʿ. The Hanafi position is clear: only actual drinking of milk from a living woman produces foster relationships.

Key Terms
رضاع (radāʿ): The suckling that establishes foster relationship causing prohibition of marriage.
لبن (laban): Milk, specifically human milk that is real milk, not moisture.
احتقان (iḥtiqān): Enema, delivering liquid into the body via the anus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does milk from a man not create radāʿ prohibition according to this passage?
A) Because it is a liquid, not milk.
B) Because it is not real milk but a moisture resembling it, like fish blood.
C) Because it comes from a man.
D) Because the child must drink from a woman's breast directly.

Key Takeaway
Only real human milk ingested by drinking within the radāʿ period creates a foster relationship; man's milk and enema do not.

Milk of a Virgin and Dead Woman in Radāʿ
Ruling with proof on milk from virgin and dead woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on milk from a virgin and a dead woman for radāʿ, and apply the condition of age and the effect of cooking on mixed milk.

Core Idea
A virgin's and dead woman's milk is real milk that prohibits marriage.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling: that the milk of a virgin and a dead woman establishes the prohibition of radāʿ (foster relationship). Many students assume that only milk from a sexually experienced, living woman counts. The Hanafi school, relying on absolute texts, extends the ruling to all women who can possibly produce milk, with a minor condition of age. We will also explore an intra-madhhab nuance regarding mixed and cooked milk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage states that prohibition is established by drinking the milk of a virgin (bikr) and a dead woman (mayyitah). Identify the specific act (shurb laban) and the hukm (haram).
The ruling is about the milk itself, not about the woman's status.
2
Examine the Proof
The proof is from absolute texts (nusus mutlaqah) that impose the prohibition on drinking any woman's milk without restriction. Understand that the Hanafi school interprets these texts broadly.
No specific verse is cited; the argument is based on the generality of the evidence.
3
Define the Virgin (Bikr)
The passage defines bikr for radāʿ as a woman who has never had intercourse (whether by marriage or fornication), even if the hymen is broken by accident, provided she is at least nine years old. Note the age condition—if under nine, the milk is not considered real milk.
Age is tied to the possibility of childbirth (wilādah).
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Mixed Milk
When milk is mixed with another substance (without cooking), Abu Yūsuf and Muḥammad consider the principle of predominance (ghalaba): if the mixture is predominantly milk, prohibition attaches; otherwise not. Abu Hanīfa’s view is not explicitly stated here, but the phrase 'according to them' implies a difference.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute; the muftā bihī for uncooked mixed milk follows the two disciples.
5
Note the Consensus on Cooked Milk
If milk is cooked with food, there is complete agreement (ittifāq) that no prohibition attaches. This overrides any other consideration.
Cooking changes the nature so that it no longer counts as milk for radāʿ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحرم بلبن البكر، والميتة. قوله : وحرم ؛ ووجهه أن نصوص حرمةِ الرضاع مطلقة شاملة لشرب لبن المرأة مطلقاً بكراً كانت أو ثيباً، حياً كانت أو ميتاً. قوله : البكر ; - بالكسر - المراد به هاهنا المرأة التي لم تجامع قط لا بنكاح ولا بسفاح ، وإن زالت بكارتها بوثبة أو مرض وقيدوها بكونها بنت تسع سنين فأكثر، فإن كانت أقل من تسع سنين فلبنها لا يحرم ؛ لأنه نصوا على أن اللبن لا يتصور إلا تما تتصوّر منه الولادة، فيحكم بأنه ليس لبناً كلبن الرجل. وعندهما تعتبر فيه الغلبة أيضاً، كما في المسائل السابقة، وهذا كله إذا كان الاختلاط بدون الطبخ، فلو طبخ اللبن مع الطعام لا يتعلق به التحريم مطلقاً اتفاقاً. كذا في «الهداية» وحواشيها.
And prohibition is established with milk of the virgin and the dead woman. He said: 'And prohibition' – its rationale is that the texts on prohibition of radāʿ are absolute, including drinking the milk of any woman, whether virgin or non-virgin, alive or dead. He said: 'the virgin' – with kasra, here meaning a woman who has never had intercourse, whether by marriage or fornication, even if her hymen has been broken by a jump or illness; and they restrict it to being nine years or older, for if she is less than nine, her milk does not cause prohibition, because they stated that milk is only conceivable from one who can conceive childbirth, so it is ruled that it is not milk like the milk of a man. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), predominance is also considered in it, as in previous issues; and all this is if the mixing is without cooking. For if milk is cooked with food, no prohibition attaches at all by agreement. Thus in Al-Hidayah and its glosses.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that milk from a virgin and from a dead woman does create radāʿ prohibition. The proof is from the absolute texts (nusūṣ) that do not differentiate based on the woman's sexual history or life status. The commentary defines 'virgin' as a woman nine years or older who has never had intercourse (even if hymen is broken by accident). If she is under nine, her milk is not considered real milk. Additionally, the passage addresses a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) regarding mixed milk: if milk is mixed with another substance, they consider predominance (ghalaba) of milk to determine if prohibition attaches. However, if milk is cooked with food, there is consensus that no prohibition attaches. The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is that cooking nullifies the effect entirely. The Hanafi school's position is that only real, unaltered milk from a woman of childbearing age creates foster relationships.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A woman who has never had sexual intercourse, regardless of hymen status, provided she is at least nine years old.
ميتة (mayyitah): A dead woman; her milk is still considered real milk for radāʿ.
غلبة (ghalaba): Predominance, used in mixed milk to determine if milk content is sufficient to cause prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for a virgin's milk to cause radāʿ prohibition?
A) The virgin must be at least nine years old.
B) The virgin must have intact hymen.
C) The virgin must never have had intercourse.
D) The milk must be consumed in a way that qualifies as radāʿ.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that any woman's milk, regardless of her sexual history or if she is deceased, causes radāʿ prohibition, provided she is of childbearing age (at least nine) and the milk is uncooked or not predominantly mixed.

Breastfeeding Co-Wife: Marital Prohibition and Financial Liability
Detailing the legal consequences when a wife breastfeeds her co-wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a wife breastfeeds her baby co-wife, identify the conditions for the husband to recover the mahr, and explain the role of intent in the financial consequence.

Core Idea
Intent determines financial liability, but the marriage prohibition is absolute once breastfeeding occurs.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from Hanafi fiqh: a wife breastfeeding her baby co-wife. The ruling covers both the marital prohibition (which is unconditional) and the financial consequences (which depend on intent). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying radāʿ laws correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and act
The act: an older wife breastfeeds her co-wife who is still in the suckling period (under two years).
2
Determine the marital ruling
Both women become permanently forbidden (haram) to the husband due to the foster relationship created.
The baby becomes his daughter; the older becomes her mother.
3
Analyze the financial consequences for each wife
The older wife gets no mahr if not consummated (she caused the annulment). The baby wife gets half the prescribed mahr (annulment before consummation, not her fault).
4
Apply the condition for recovery by the husband
The husband may recover the half-mahr from the older wife only if she intended to cause corruption (fasād), meaning she was aware and not acting out of necessity.
Conditions: she must be adult, sane, not coerced, aware, and not breastfeeding to relieve hunger or save life.
5
Understand the talil (reasoning)
The breastfeeding creates foster relationships analogous to natural ones: the baby becomes his daughter, the older becomes mother of his daughter, prohibiting marriage.
The milk must be from the husband or from a wife he has consummated?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أرضعت ضرَّتَها حَرُمَتا ، ولا مهر للكبيرة إن لم توطأ، وللرضيعة نصفه، ورجع به على المرضعة إن قصدت الفساد وإلا فلا. قوله : وإن أرضعت ... الخ ; حاصله : أنه إذا كان لرجل زوجتان كبيرة وصغيرة، فأرضعت الكبيرة الصغيرة في مدة رضاعتها، حرمنا على الزوج ; لصيرورة الصغيرة بنته إن كان لبن المرضعة منه أو بنتِ مدخولته وصيرورة الكبيرة أم بنته أو أم معقودته . قوله: نصفه ; لكون الفرقة قبل الدخول وعدم مجيء الفرقة من قبلها. قوله : ورجع ; أي رجع الزوج بما أدّاه إلى الصغيرة على الكبيرة إن تعمدت الفساد بأن كانت عاقلة غير مكرهة، متيقظة عالمة بأصل النكاح، وبإفساد الإرضاع ، ولم تقصد دفع جوع أو هلاك.
And if she breastfeeds her co-wife, both become forbidden (to the husband), and there is no dower (mahr) for the older wife if she was not consummated, and for the baby half of it, and he recovers it from the breastfeeding wife if she intended corruption, otherwise no. He said: 'And if she breastfeeds...' its summary: if a man has two wives, an older and a young one, and the older breastfeeds the young during her suckling period, both become forbidden to the husband because the young becomes his daughter if the milk is from him (the husband) or from his consummated wife, and the older becomes the mother of his daughter or the mother of his betrothed. He said: 'half of it' because the separation occurred before consummation and not initiated by her. He said: 'and he recovers' meaning the husband recovers what he paid to the young from the older if she deliberately caused corruption, being sane, not coerced, alert, knowing the marriage and that breastfeeding causes corruption, and not intending to relieve hunger or save from death.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing a complex radāʿ scenario. The ruling: if a man has two wives, one older and one a baby (a co-wife in suckling period), and the older wife breastfeeds the baby, both women become permanently forbidden to the husband. The reasoning (tālīl) is that the baby becomes the husband's daughter (if the milk is from him or from a wife he has consummated), and the older wife becomes the mother of that daughter, creating a direct foster relationship. The financial consequences: the older wife gets no mahr if the marriage was not consummated (since the prohibition arose from her action), and the baby gets half the prescribed mahr (because separation occurred before consummation). The husband can recover that half from the breastfeeding wife if she intended to cause the corruption (فساد) - i.e., she was aware of the marital relationship and that breastfeeding would break it, and she did not breastfeed out of necessity to save the baby's life. The conditions for recovery: she must be adult, sane, not coerced, aware of the marriage and the effect of breastfeeding, and not acting to prevent hunger or death. If she acted with good intent, the husband does not recover. This ruling safeguards the integrity of foster relationships and rights of parties.

Key Terms
ضرَّة (ḍarrāh): Co-wife, a woman who is married to the same man as another woman.
فساد (fasād): Corruption, here meaning deliberate intent to break the marriage through breastfeeding.
مهر (mahr): Dower, the obligatory payment from husband to wife upon marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the husband recover the half-mahr from the breastfeeding older wife?
A) Always, because she caused the marriage to be forbidden.
B) Only if she intended to cause corruption (فساد) and was aware.
C) Only if the baby dies.
D) Never, because the mahr is due to the wife.

Key Takeaway
The marital prohibition from radāʿ is absolute, but financial liability hinges on the intent behind the breastfeeding act.

Proof of Radāʿ: Required Witness Testimony
Stating the evidentiary requirement for radāʿ with analogy to property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness requirements for proving radāʿ and explain the analogy to property claims.

Core Idea
Radāʿ is proven by the same witness standard as financial claims: two men or one man and two women.

Radāʿ (foster relationship) has serious legal consequences, such as prohibiting marriage between the nursing child and the foster family. To ensure certainty, the Hanafi school requires the same level of proof as for property claims. This lesson examines the specific witness requirement and its basis in qiyas (analogy).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first line: 'And its proof is two men, or one man and two women.' This is the central ruling of the passage.
The ruling is a direct statement of the required witness combination.
2
Recognize the analogy
The next part states that radāʿ is established 'by that by which property is established.' This indicates qiyas (analogy) to financial claims.
The basis is the Quranic verses on testimony (e.g., 2:282).
3
Understand the scope
The passage explicitly excludes a single woman's testimony, even if she is the nursing mother, before or after marriage. Note the reason: certainty is required to avoid false claims.
The nursing mother is not a sufficient witness on her own.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow a single woman's testimony for radāʿ. The Hanafi view is stricter, considering it analogous to property.
This difference has practical implications in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجته رجلان، أو رجل وامرأتان. قوله : وحجته ; أي الرضاع، يعني أنّ الرضاع إنما يثبت بما يثبت به المال من شهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، فلا تثبت بشهادة امرأة واحدة فقط ولو كانت مرضعة سواء كانت شهادتها قبل النكاح أو بعده.
And its proof is two men, or one man and two women. He said: 'And its proof' i.e., of radāʿ, meaning that radāʿ is only established by that by which property is established: the testimony of two men or one man and two women. So it is not established by the testimony of only one woman, even if she is the nursing woman, whether her testimony is before the marriage or after it.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the evidence required to establish radāʿ (foster relationship). The ruling is that radāʿ is proven by the same standard as financial claims: two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses. This is based on analogy (qiyās jaliy) to property matters, because radāʿ affects marriage rights which are similar to property rights. A single woman's testimony is insufficient, even if she is the one who breastfed and even if she testifies before the marriage (as a warning) or after. The commentator emphasizes that the nursing mother alone cannot prove radāʿ; she needs corroboration. This ruling safeguards against false claims that could disrupt marriages. The Hanafi school is strict on witness requirements for radāʿ due to the seriousness of altering marital relationships.

Key Terms
حجة (ḥujjah): Proof, evidence; here specifically the witness testimony required to establish radāʿ.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony in court; for radāʿ, two men or one man and two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two women.
C) Two men or one man and two women.
D) One man.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, radāʿ is proven by the same witness standard as property claims: two men or one man and two women.

Definition and Conditions of Zihar (Uzihar)
Defining zihar and its essential conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of zihar, identify its essential conditions, and distinguish valid from invalid likening statements.

Core Idea
Zihar is a prohibited comparison of one's wife to a female mahram's concealed organ; invalid if the target is male or non-prohibited.

Zihar is a unique form of marital prohibition in Islamic law, rooted in the Quranic verses of Surah al-Mujadilah. The Hanafi school defines it precisely as a likening of one's wife to a mahram relative's prohibited organ. This lesson unpacks that definition, exploring who may perform it, to whom, and which statements trigger the ruling. A key intra-Hanafi disagreement about likening to male mahrams illustrates the school's careful casuistry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its core definition
The passage defines zihar as tashbih (likening) of one's wife. Note that it excludes slave women and non-Muslims, and the likening can be explicit or implicit.
2
Analyze the conditions of the speaker
The speaker must be Muslim, sane, adult, and the statement must be intentional. Some cases (intoxicated, coerced, mute) are valid due to deterrence or necessity.
Zihar of a dhimmi or minor is invalid.
3
Examine the object of likening
The likening must be to an organ of a mahram (perpetually forbidden relative) that is prohibited to view. Likening to non-mahram organs (leg, hand) or to an undetermined part (juz' sha'i') is valid, but not a specific non-prohibited organ.
Also valid: likening to the whole mahram (first priority).
4
Distinguish valid and invalid formulations
Valid: 'You are like the back of my mother' (or similar). Invalid: 'You are my mother' (no tashbih) or 'You are like my sister's hand' (hand not prohibited).
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on male mahrams
al-Bahr allows likening to male mahrams based on general wording. al-Nahr/al-Bada'i restrict to female mahrams, which is the mufta bihi position.
Practical consequence: if a man says 'You are like my father's back', the preferred view says no zihar.

Chapter of Zihar: (It is likening his wife) ... The origin in this chapter is His statement, Exalted is He, in Surah al-Mujadilah: 'Indeed Allah has heard the statement of the woman who argues with you concerning her husband and complains to Allah...' The verses were revealed when Aws ibn Samit practiced zihar on his wife and she came complaining to the Messenger of Allah, as recorded by al-Hakim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah and others in detail. He said: 'It is likening his wife' – an addition to the object, and by this he excludes his slave woman, so there is no zihar with her legally, as will come. The meaning of likening is general, whether explicit or implicit, as if ... or what expresses her, or an undetermined part of her with an organ whose sight is prohibited from among the organs of his mahram relatives. ... If a man's wife said to him: 'You are to me like so-and-so,' intending that, and it includes, by its generality, immediate zihar and that suspended on her will, or temporary for a day or a month. And he excludes phrases like: 'You are my mother' without likening, for it is meaningless speech and not zihar. The meaning of likening is the likening of a Muslim, for there is no zihar for a dhimmi according to us. And the meaning of Muslim is the sane, adult, so the zihar of an insane person, a minor, an idiot, a bewildered one, an unconscious one, and a sleeping one is invalid. But it is valid from an intoxicated person as a deterrent, and from one who errs, one who is coerced, and a mute by his understandable gesture. This is in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Nahr'. He said: 'or what expresses' i.e. likening what expresses the essence from among the organs like the face and head. He said: 'or a part' i.e. an undetermined part of the wife, like half of you or a third of you, and he excludes likening an unshared part that does not express the whole like the belly and thigh. He said: 'with an organ' attached to the likening, i.e. with an organ from among the organs of his mahram whose sight is prohibited, and likening her to the whole of them is a fortiori zihar. He said: 'whose sight is prohibited to him' – excluding the leg, hand, and other organs that it is permissible to look at, for likening her to them is not zihar. He said: 'his mahram' – with fatha, plural of mahram: one whom it is forbidden to marry perpetually. He said: 'his mahram' – its apparent meaning includes male and female, so if he likened her to his father's private part, he would be a mazahir. This is in 'al-Bahr', but it is rejected in 'al-Nahr' by what is in 'al-Bada'i' that among the conditions of zihar is that the object of zihar be of the class of women, so if he likened her to his father's back or his son's back, it is not valid, because it is only known...
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the chapter of zihar (uzihar) from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. The author begins by explaining the placement of this chapter after khula': both typically arise from nushuz (marital discord), but khula' is stronger in prohibition as it actually dissolves the marriage, so it is placed first. He defines zihar linguistically as a verbal noun from 'zahara' meaning when a man says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' The primary textual basis is the verses from Surah al-Mujadilah (1-4), which were revealed concerning Aws ibn Samit and his wife Khawlah, as narrated in hadith collections. The definition of zihar in law is 'likening one's wife' (tashbih zawjatih). The author notes that this excludes a female slave; zihar does not occur with a slave woman, as will be explained later. The likening can be explicit or implicit, such as saying 'You are like so-and-so' intending the meaning. It can be immediate, conditional upon her will, or temporary. He then lists conditions: the speaker must be a Muslim (no zihar for dhimmis), sane and adult (zihar of an insane person, minor, etc. is invalid). However, zihar is valid from an intoxicated person as a deterrent, from one who errs, one coerced, and a mute by his understandable gesture. The likening must be to an organ whose sight is prohibited to him from among his mahram relatives (those permanently forbidden in marriage). Likening to non-mahram organs like leg or hand is not zihar. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute at the end: according to 'al-Bahr', likening to a male mahram's organ (e.g., father's private part) constitutes zihar based on the general wording 'mahram.' But 'al-Nahr' rejects this, citing 'al-Bada'i' that the object of likening must be from the class of women, so likening to a male is invalid. This illustrates that the Hanafi school requires the likening to be to a female mahram relative, though the exact scope is debated among later authorities.

Key Terms
الظهار (al-zihar): A man's statement to his wife likening her to a mahram relative (e.g., 'You are like my mother's back'), which triggers prohibition of marital relations until expiation is performed.
تشبيه (tashbih): Explicit or implicit comparison of the wife to a mahram relative in a prohibited manner.
محارم (mahārim): Relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood, suckling, or marriage ties.
جزء شائع (juz' shā'i'): An undetermined part that can express the whole, like 'half of you'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A man says to his wife: 'You are to me like my father's back.'
B) A man says to his wife: 'You are my mother.'
C) A man says to his wife: 'You are to me like your hand.'
D) A man says to his wife: 'You are to me like the back of my mother.'

Key Takeaway
Zihar requires a comparison of one's wife to a female mahram's concealed organ; invalid comparisons include non-prohibited organs, lack of tashbih, or male mahrams per the preferred view.

Categories Disqualified for Expiatory Emancipation
List of disqualified categories for kafara emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which slaves are disqualified for expiatory emancipation (kafara) based on the Hanafi criterion of fā'it jins al-manfa'ah and apply the ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A slave is invalid for kafara if the entire kind of benefit is permanently lost, not just a defect.

Expiatory emancipation (kafara) requires a specific type of slave. Not every slave fulfills the obligation. Hanafi fiqh defines a precise disqualification: the slave must not have lost the entire kind of benefit (fā'it jins al-manfa'ah). In this lesson, we examine which physical incapacities meet this criterion and also cover other categories like mudabbar and mukatab that are automatically disqualified. Understanding these rules ensures that the expiation is legally valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Criterion
The key disqualifying condition is 'fā'it jins al-manfa'ah' – permanent loss of the entire kind of benefit from the slave. Distinguish this from mere defects or impairments.
Temporary conditions do not disqualify.
2
List the Physical Incapacities
From the text, list: blind, permanently insane, missing both hands, missing both thumbs (hands), missing both feet, missing one hand and one foot from the same side. Note that losing one hand, one foot, or one eye is not disqualifying.
The thumbs are essential for grip; foot thumbs are not.
3
Distinguish Permanent vs. Temporary
The commentary clarifies that a person who is sometimes insane and sometimes sane is not disqualified because the loss is not permanent. Apply this principle to other conditions.
Permanence is key.
4
Identify Non-Physical Disqualifications
The text lists: mudabbar (promised freedom upon death), mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba, buying a mahram relative with intent of kafara, and emancipating half a slave then the rest in two acts.
For mudabbar and umm walad, slavery is defective; for mukatab, emancipation becomes a transaction.
5
Apply the Ruling
Given a slave, check if he falls into any disqualified category. If not, the slave is valid for kafara. If disqualified, the expiation is not fulfilled.
Always verify ownership and absence of disqualifying conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۲) قوله : احترازاً ; فإن من يصيرُ مجنوناً أحياناً وتحصل له إفاقة منه أحياناً يجوز ; المنفعة. لأنه ليس فائت جنس [۳] قوله : أو إبهاماه ; الأولى أن يقول : أو إبهاماهما ; ليفيد قطع إبهامي اليدين ; لان قطع إبهامي الرجلين غير مانع، وإنما لم يجز عنق هؤلاء ; لأن الفائت فيهم جنس المنفعة المقصودة، والمانع هو فوتُ جنس المنفعة دون اختلاله ونقصانه. فالأعمى فائت منفعة البصر، والأعور مختلها، ومقطوع اليدين أو الرجلين أو يد ورجل من جانب واحد يفوت فيه نفع المشي، بخلافِ مقطوع إحدى اليدين أو الرجلين أو مقطوع اليد والرجل من خلاف، فإنّ المشي هناك ممكن، ومقطوع إبهامي اليدين يفوت فيه جنس المنفعة ; لأنَّ قوّة البطش بهما، بخلاف إبهامي الرجلين. [٤] قوله : ولا مدبّر ... الخ ; وجه عدم إجزاء المدبّر، وكذا أم الولد أنهما استحقا الحرية بجهة التدبير والاستيلاد فكان الرق فيهما ناقصاً، ووجه عدم إجزاء المكاتب الذي أدى بعض البدل أن إعتاقه لا يكون قربة محضة، بل يكون بعوض، بخلاف ما إذا لو يؤدِّ شيئاً، فإنّ عتقه لا يكون بعوض، والرق فيه كامل ما بقي عليه درهم. Not one who has lost the kind of benefit: like the blind, the permanently insane, the one whose hands are cut off, or his two thumbs, or his two feet, or a hand and a foot from one side; and not a mudabbar, nor a mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba, and a mukatab who has not paid anything, and buying his relative with the intention of his expiation, and emancipating half his slave then the rest of him. Not one who has lost the kind of benefit: like the blind, the permanently insane — as a precaution against one who becomes insane and recovers — and the one whose hands are cut off, or his two thumbs, or his two feet, or a hand and a foot from one side; and not a mudabbar, nor a mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba. [Commentary:] His saying 'and buying': meaning purchasing a relative (who is a mahram) from him with the intention of expiation, for the relative becomes free at the time of purchase, and likewise everything in which he has a part such as accepting a gift or charity. His saying 'as a precaution': for one who becomes insane sometimes and then recovers is permissible; because he is not one who has lost the kind of benefit. His saying 'or his two thumbs': the first should say 'or his two thumbs' to indicate cutting off the thumbs of both hands; because cutting off the thumbs of both feet is not a preventer. These are not permissible for emancipation because the loss for them is of the kind of intended benefit, and the preventer is the loss of the kind of benefit not its defect or deficiency. The blind has lost the benefit of sight, the one-eyed has a defect in it; the one with both hands, feet, or a hand and foot from one side loses the benefit of walking, unlike the one with one hand, one foot, or a hand and foot from opposite sides, for walking is possible there; the one with both thumbs cut off loses the kind of benefit because the power of gripping is with them, unlike the thumbs of both feet. His saying 'and not a mudabbar...': the reason for the mudabbar not being valid, and similarly umm al-walad, is that they have become entitled to freedom through tadbir or istilad, so slavery in them is defective. The reason for the mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba not being valid is that his emancipation is not purely a good deed but is for consideration, unlike one who has paid nothing, for his emancipation is not for consideration and his slavery is complete as long as a dirham remains. (1) Meaning before intercourse with the one from whom he has made zihar; because he emancipated with two statements, and deficiency remains in his ownership due to the cause of expiation, and that does not prevent permissibility. See: Majma' al-Anhur (1:451). (2) Because the power of gripping is with them, so losing them means losing the kind of benefit. See: Al-Hidayah (2:20).
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling: it explains who is disqualified from being used for expiatory emancipation (kafara) in Hanafi fiqh. The key category is 'fā'it jins al-manfa'ah' – one who has permanently lost the entire kind of benefit from the slave. Examples include the blind (loss of sight), the permanently insane (loss of reason), and those with missing hands, thumbs, feet, or a hand and foot from one side (loss of movement/grip). The commentator clarifies that temporary insanity does not disqualify. The thumbs of the hands are specified because they are essential for grip; thumbs of the feet are not a barrier. The ruling then lists additional categories that are not valid: mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon master's death), mukatab (a slave who has paid part of his kitaba), and the case of a master buying his mahram relative with the intention of kafara (the relative becomes free upon purchase and thus cannot be used). Also, emancipating half a slave and then the rest in two separate acts is not valid because the first act creates a deficiency. The commentary provides reasons: for mudabbar and umm al-walad, slavery is already defective because they have a right to freedom; for the mukatab who has paid part, emancipation is not purely a good deed (qurba mahda) because it involves consideration. The ruling distinguishes based on the completeness of the malik's ownership and the nature of the benefit lost.

Key Terms
فائت جنس المنفعة (fā'it jins al-manfa'ah): One who has lost the entire kind of benefit from a slave, not just a defect or impairment.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death.
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has contracted a kitaba (written agreement) to purchase his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following slaves is NOT disqualified for expiatory emancipation according to the Hanafi school?
A) A blind slave
B) A one-eyed slave
C) A mudabbar slave
D) A slave missing both hands

Key Takeaway
Only a slave whose entire kind of benefit is permanently intact and whose slavery is full and unconditional can be used for expiatory emancipation (kafara).

Emancipating Half a Slave for Kafara: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on half-emancipation of jointly owned and personal slaves with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on emancipating half a jointly owned slave for kafara and explain the practical consequence of their difference.

Core Idea
Emancipating half a jointly owned slave for kafara is invalid per Abu Hanifa, even if the other half is later guaranteed.

In the Hanafi school, expiatory kafara requires a complete slave. But what if someone emancipates only half of a jointly owned slave and then guarantees the other half? The Imams differ: Abu Hanifa rules it invalid because the initial act creates a defect, while the two Companions (Sahibayn) allow it if the emancipator is wealthy. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the practical effect on fulfilling kafara.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and issue
The act is emancipating half of a jointly owned slave with the intention of kafara, then later guaranteeing the partner's share. The issue: does this fulfill the kafara obligation?
Kafara requires a complete, defect-free slave; partial emancipation may be considered deficient.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds it invalid. His reasoning: the first half impairs the partner's share (intaqaṣa naṣīb ṣāḥibihi), making the slave defective. The subsequent guarantee does not retroactively cure the defect at the moment of emancipation.
The defect is created at the time of the first act, and the ruling follows the initial state.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it valid if the emancipator is wealthy. Their reasoning: emancipation is indivisible (lā yatajazzā); by guaranteeing the other half, he becomes owner of the whole, so the first half counts as full emancipation. If insolvent, the slave must work (sa'āyah), making it a transaction and thus not valid.
The key principle for them is that emancipation is indivisible; the act is judged by its final outcome.
4
Identify the contested principle
The disagreement hinges on whether emancipation is divisible for kafara. Abu Hanifa considers the immediate effect; the Sahibayn consider the eventual outcome. Also, the role of the defect at the time of the first act.
This is a usul al-fiqh difference: 'al-amr al-mujzi' vs. 'al-amr al-mujzi bi al-taba'?'
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, following Abu Hanifa, the kafara is not fulfilled; according to the Sahibayn, it is fulfilled if the emancipator is wealthy. The matn sides with Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn's view is a valid alternative.
The mufta bihi is typically Abu Hanifa's view, but some later scholars may give fatwa based on need.

Source Text

And [the ruling on] emancipating half a jointly owned slave, then the rest of him after guaranteeing [the other half] — because he impaired the share of his partner in his ownership, then it transfers to the ownership of the emancipator by guarantee. According to them [the two Companions], it is permissible if the emancipator is wealthy, because he owns his partner's share by guarantee, so it is as if he emancipated the whole for expiation, unlike if he is insolvent; in that case, according to them, the slave must work to pay for the partner's share, so it becomes an emancipation for compensation. And [the ruling on] half his slave for his expiation, then the rest of him after intercourse with the one from whom he performed zihar — because emancipation. [Commentary:] His saying 'and emancipating...': meaning if he emancipates half of a slave jointly owned between him and another, while he is wealthy, and he guarantees his partner's half and owns it by guarantee, then emancipates, such emancipation does not count for his expiation. His saying 'because...': its gist is that when he emancipated half, the other half which is in the ownership of his partner becomes defective and impaired due to the impossibility of maintaining slavery in it because of the sanctity of [the emancipated] half; therefore, the emancipator must guarantee it if he is wealthy, and the slave must work to pay the value of his half to become completely free; after it becomes defective, it transfers to the emancipator's ownership by guarantee, so such [emancipation] does not fulfill the expiation. His saying 'unlike...': it is said in Al-'Inayah: if it is asked, 'It should count as expiation according to them even if the emancipator is insolvent, because the slave becomes a free man in debt, based on the principle that emancipation is indivisible according to them.' The answer: it is not valid because the obligation of this debt arises from the emancipation, so this emancipation is not gratuitous and thus does not count for expiation. His saying 'and half...': meaning it is not permissible to emancipate half his slave with the intention of expiation, then [the rest] — (1) Due to the impossibility of maintaining ownership in it, then what remains transfers to him by guarantee, so in meaning it is emancipation of a slave except something, and similar prevents expiation. See: Al-'Inayah (4:264). (2) Because emancipation is indivisible according to them. See: Al-Tabyin (3:9). (3) Al-'Inayah (4:264).
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of emancipating half a slave (either jointly owned or one's own) for expiatory kafara. The matn states that emancipating half a jointly owned slave and then the rest after guaranteeing the other half is not valid. The reason given is that the first emancipation creates a deficiency in the co-owner's share, which then transfers to the emancipator by guarantee; thus the emancipation is not from a complete ownership. However, the two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is valid if the emancipator is wealthy, because he comes to own the entire slave through guarantee, and in their view emancipation is indivisible (lā yatajazzā) so the first half counts as a full emancipation. If the emancipator is insolvent, they too require the slave to work (sa'āyah) for the partner's share, making the emancipation a transaction, so it does not count for kafara. The commentary then addresses a potential objection: why doesn't it count even for the wealthy? The answer: because the deficiency still existed at the time of the first half. For the case of emancipating half of one's own slave, the ruling is similar: it is not valid because the first half creates a deficiency in the slave, and the second half after intercourse (with the zihar wife) is considered a separate act; the slave is not fully owned as a complete slave at the time of the first act. The underlying principle is that for kafara, the emancipation must be of a complete, undiminished slave whose benefit is fully available.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee or liability to pay the value of the co-owner's share in a jointly owned slave.
سعاية (sa'āyah): The slave's working to earn money to pay off the partner's share in his value.
لا يتجزأ (lā yatajazzā): Indivisible; used by Sahibayn to support that emancipating half is like emancipating the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider the emancipation of half a jointly owned slave valid for kafara?
A) If the emancipator is insolvent and the slave works to compensate
B) If the emancipator is wealthy and guarantees the partner's share
C) If the emancipator emancipates the second half immediately
D) If the slave agrees to be used for kafara

Key Takeaway
The validity of half-emancipation for kafara depends on the principle of indivisibility of emancipation; the Hanafi school's authoritative position is that it is invalid due to the defect created at the initial act.

Feeding in Expiation: Tamleek vs Ibahah
Explains conditions for valid feeding in kafarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tamleek and ibahah in feeding for kafarah and state the specific requirements for each method.

Core Idea
Feeding in expiation requires either ownership transfer (tamleek) with minimum fitrah, or satiation (ibahah) with two meals—but never a single-day lump sum by ibahah.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary expands on the method of fulfilling the obligation of feeding in expiation (kafarah). It clarifies that feeding can be done by either making the recipient the owner of the food (tamleek) or merely making the food available for consumption (ibahah). Each method has distinct conditions: tamleek requires a minimum amount equal to fitrah per person, while ibahah requires providing two meals and ensuring satiation, regardless of how little the recipients actually eat. The passage also addresses mixing different grains and the validity of giving one poor person the entire expiation over multiple days versus in a single day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods and key terms
Locate the terms 'tamleek' (making owner) and 'ibahah' (making available). Understand that these are the two valid ways to feed in kafarah according to the Hanafi school.
The Shafi'i school only accepts tamleek.
2
Distinguish the requirements for each method
For tamleek, the minimum is the amount of fitrah (e.g., half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley). For ibahah, the requirement is to provide two meals (lunch and supper) and ensure the recipients are satiated, even if they eat little.
A weaned child does not count as they cannot eat the customary amount.
3
Understand the rule on mixing grains
The text states it is permissible to give a quarter sa' of wheat with half a sa' of dates or barley because they share the same purpose (issuing food to satisfy hunger). However, mixing different categories (e.g., feeding and clothing) is not allowed.
This applies to tamleek when combining different grains to reach the required quantity.
4
Analyze the dispute on giving one person the full amount in one day
Giving all sixty days' worth of food to one poor person in one day by ibahah is unanimously invalid because there is no multiplicity in reality or legally. For tamleek, there is an ikhtilaf: some scholars say it does not suffice (the need for ownership is not renewed in one day), while others say it suffices (the need for tamleek can be renewed).
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it suffices by tamleek but not by ibahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قل ما أكلوا ، أو أعطى من بُرّ ومن تمر أو شعير، أو واحداً شهرين جاز، وفي يوم واحد قدر الشهرين لا يجوز إلا عن يومه. والتعشية، والغداء طعام الصبح ، والعشاء بالفتح طعام المساء، وحاصله : إن الإطعام إن كان بطريق التمليك يجب إعطاء قدر الفطرة، وإن كان بطريق الإباحة يجب التغدية والتعشية مع إشباعهم في الوقتين، وإن قل مأكولهم. قوله : وإن ؛ الواو وصليّة، والحاصل أنه لا بُدَّ في التمليك أن لا ينقص عن مقدار الفطرة، وأمّا في الإباحة فالمعتبر هو إشباعهم، وإن أكلوا قليلاً، نعم لو كان فيمن أطعمهم صبي فطيم لم يجزه ؛ لأنه لا يستوفي القدر المعتاد. كذا في «منح الغفار». قوله : أو أعطى...الخ ؛ يعني يجوز أن يعطي ربع الصاع من الحنطة مع نصف صاع من تمر أو شعير، فيكمل أحدهما بالآخر ؛ لكون الجنس متحداً من حيث المقصود، وهو الإطعام وسدّ الجوع ، وأما إذا اختلف الجنس فلا يجوز تكميل أحدهما بالآخر، كما إذا أطعم خمسة مساكين في كفّارة اليمين بطريق الإباحة، وكسى خمسة. كذا في «النهاية». قوله : أو واحداً ...الخ ؛ يعني يجوز أن يعطي فقيراً واحداً مقدار الفطرة ستين يوماً ؛ لأنَّ المقصود سدّ حاجة المحتاج ، والحاجة تتجدّد في كلّ يوم، فالدفع إليه في اليوم الثاني كالدفع إلى غيره ، فيصير كأنه أعطى ستين مسكيناً، وفي قول المصنف له شهرين تسامح، فإنّ الشهرين ربّما يكونان ناقصين، فيصير المجموع ثمانية وخمسين يوماً. قوله : لا ؛ هذا في الإباحة اتفاقي، وفي التمليك خلافي، يعني إذا دفع المسكين واحد في يوم واحد ستين مرّة بطريق الإباحة، فلا خلاف لأحد في عدم جوازه ؛ لعدمِ وجود التعدّد لا حقيقة ولا حكماً. وإن كان ذلك بطريق التمليك ، فقال بعض المشايخ: لا يجزئه ؛ لأنَّ المقصود سد الحاجة ؛ ولهذا لا يجوز الصرف إلى الغني، وبعد ما استوفى وظيفة اليوم لم تبق له حاجة إلى الأخرى، فلم يكن في صرف الباقي إليه سد الحاجة. وقيل : يجزئه ؛ لأن الحاجة إلى التمليك قد تتجدّد في يوم واحد، بخلاف حاجة إباحة الطعام، فإنّها لا تتجدّد في يوم واحد. كذا في «العناية».
And if what they ate is little, or he gave some wheat and some dates or barley, or one person for two months, it is permissible; and in one day the amount of two months is not permissible except for that day. And al-tashiyah (supper), and al-ghada' (lunch) is the morning meal, and al-asha' (with fatha) is the evening meal. The summary: feeding, if by way of tamleek (making owner), it is obligatory to give the amount of fitrah; and if by way of ibahah (making available), it is obligatory to provide lunch and supper with satiating them at both times, even if their food is little. [Commentary:] And the conclusion is that in tamleek it must not be less than the amount of fitrah; as for ibahah, the consideration is satiating them, even if they eat little. Yes, if among those he feeds there is a recently weaned child, it does not suffice him because he does not consume the customary amount. Likewise in al-Nihayah. [Commentary:] It means it is permissible to give one poor person the amount of fitrah for sixty days because the purpose is fulfilling the need of the needy, and need is renewed every day, so giving him on the second day is like giving to another, so it becomes as if he gave sixty poor people; and the author's saying 'two months' is a looseness, for the two months might be deficient, so the total becomes fifty-eight days. [Commentary:] This is agreed upon in ibahah, and disputed in tamleek: meaning if he gives one poor person sixty times in one day by way of ibahah, there is no disagreement on its invalidity due to lack of multiplicity in reality or legally. And if that was by way of tamleek, then some mashayikh said: it does not suffice him because the purpose is fulfilling need, and after he has fulfilled the function of the day, he has no need for another, so there is no fulfilling of need in giving the rest to him. And it is said: it suffices him because the need for tamleek may be renewed in one day, unlike the need for ibahah of food, which is not renewed in one day. Likewise in al-Inayah.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with explanatory commentary on the method of fulfilling the obligation of feeding in expiation (kafarah) or charity. The author clarifies two distinct methods: tamleek (making the recipient the owner of the food) and ibahah (making the food available for consumption without transfer of ownership). In tamleek, the minimum is the amount of fitrah per person; in ibahah, the requirement is to provide two meals (lunch and supper) and ensure satiation, regardless of how little the recipients actually eat. A weaned child does not count as they cannot eat enough. The passage also addresses mixing types of grains: giving a quarter sa' of wheat with half a sa' of dates or barley is permissible because they share the same purpose of satiation, but different purposes (e.g., feeding vs. clothing) cannot be combined. Giving one poor person the amount for sixty days over multiple days is valid because the need renews daily; giving it all in one day is invalid for ibahah due to lack of multiplicity, but disputed for tamleek. Some scholars say it does not suffice because the need for ownership is not renewed in one day; others say it suffices because the need for tamleek can be renewed.

Key Terms
الإطعام (al-it'am): Feeding the poor in expiation; can be by tamleek (making owner) or ibahah (making available).
التمليك (al-tamleek): Making the recipient the owner of the food by transferring ownership.
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Making the food available for the recipient to eat without transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He gives each poor person half a sa' of wheat.
B) He provides two meals (lunch and supper) and ensures they are satiated.
C) He gives the food to the poor and transfers ownership.
D) He gives the poor the monetary value of the food.

Key Takeaway
Feeding in kafarah can be done by tamleek (minimum fitrah per person) or ibahah (two meals with satiation); giving all in one day to one person is invalid by ibahah but permissible by tamleek per the mufta bihi.

Tamleek vs. Ibahah in Feeding Kafarah: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on feeding in kafarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the method of feeding in kafarah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on dalalat al-nass.

Core Idea
Feeding (it'am) means making someone eat, not making them own — ibahah suffices.

When a Muslim must feed the poor as expiation (kafarah), an important question arises: does the feeding require transferring ownership of the food (tamleek), or is it enough to make the food available for them to eat (ibahah)? This dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools has real practical consequences. In this lesson, we will dive into the linguistic and usul arguments, focusing on how the Hanafis derive their position using the principle of dalalat al-nass.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the precise legal question: In feeding kafarah (e.g., for a broken oath), what method fulfills the Quranic command 'feeding ten poor people'?
The verse is Quran 5:89.
2
Identify both positions
Clearly state the Hanafi position (ibahah and tamleek both valid) and the Shafi'i position (tamleek only).
The Hanafi position is presented as 'this is our madhhab'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the linguistic argument: 'it'am' derives from 'ta'm' (eating), so it means making someone a ta'im (eater). This is achieved by ibahah. Tamleek is only added by implication (dalala) because it serves the broader purpose of fulfilling needs.
The usul principle used is dalalat al-nass, where the text indicates a ruling beyond its literal wording.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school draws an analogy with clothing (kiswah) mentioned in the same verse, where tamleek is required by consensus. They argue that feeding should be treated similarly.
The Hanafi response distinguishes: clothing (a physical object) necessarily implies ownership, while food (consumable) does not.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply the difference: A Hanafi can fulfill the obligation by inviting sixty poor people to a meal; a Shafi'i must give each poor person ownership of the food (e.g., a meal packet).
The text states the Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي أعطى شخصاً واحداً في يوم واحد قدر الشهرين لا يجوز إلا عن هذا اليوم. قوله : شخصاً واحداً ; وأما لو أعطى ستين مسكيناً في يوم واحدٍ فلا شبهة في جوازه ، فإنّ المفروض هو إطعام ستين مسكيناً بدفعة كانت أو بدفعات. قوله : هذا ; إشارة إلى ما فهم من المسائل السابقة أنه يجوز الإطعام بطريق الإباحة، وبطريق التمليك كليهما. هذا مذهبنا ، وأما عند الشَّافِعِي رضي الله عنه فلا بُدَّ من التمليك، كما في الكسوة، ووجه قولنا : ما ذُكِرَ في أصول الفقهِ في دلالةِ النَّص : إن الإطعام جعلُ الغيرِ طاعماً، وهو بالإباحة... إلى آخره. قوله : من التمليك ; أي جعله مالكاً بإعطائه كما في الكسوة لا بدّ منه اتفاقاً، فلا تكفي في الإطعام الإباحة. قوله : جعل الغير طاعماً ; أي اكلاً ; لأنَّ حقيقة طعمت الطعام أكلته ، والهمزة للتعدية إلى المفعول الثاني ; أي جعلته أكلاً. قوله : إلى آخره ; أي إلى آخر التقرير المذكور في كتب أصول الفقه، الشارح له في «التنقيح» في التقسيم الرابع ، عند ذكر أمثلة إشارة النص : «وكقوله : إطْعَامُ عَشَرَة مَسَكِينَ، فيه إشارة إلى أنّ الأصل هو الإباحة، والتمليك ملحق به ؛ لأن الإطعام جعل الغير طاعماً لا جعله مالكاً. وألحق به التمليك دلالة ؛ لأنَّ المقصود قضاء حوائجهم، وهي كثيرة، فأقيم التمليك مقامها، ولا كذلك في الكسوة ; لأنّ الكسوة - بالكسر – الثوب، فوجب أن
That is, if he gives one person in one day the amount of two months, it is not permissible except for this day. [Commentary on] his saying: one person; and if he gave sixty poor people in one day, there is no doubt about its permissibility, for the assumption is feeding sixty poor people, whether in one go or in multiple payments. [Commentary on] his saying: this; reference to what is understood from the previous issues that feeding is permissible by way of ibahah and by way of tamleek, both. This is our madhhab; and according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, tamleek is necessary, as in clothing. And the basis of our statement: what was mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh regarding the indication of the text: that feeding (it'am) is making another person a taim (one who eats), and that is by ibahah... etc. [Commentary on] his saying: from tamleek; that is, making him the owner by giving it, as in clothing, it is necessary by agreement, so ibahah is not sufficient in feeding. [Commentary on] his saying: making another a taim; that is, one who eats, because the literal meaning of 'ta'imtu al-ta'ama' is 'I ate the food', and the hamza is for ta'diyah (transitivity) to the second object, i.e., I made him eat it. [Commentary on] his saying: etc.; that is, up to the end of the discussion mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh books; the commentator explained it in al-Tanqih in the fourth division, when mentioning examples of the indication of the text: 'like His saying: feeding ten poor people', in it is an indication that the basis is ibahah, and tamleek is annexed to it, because feeding is making another a taim, not making him a malik. And tamleek is annexed to it by implication, because the purpose is fulfilling their needs, which are many, so tamleek is made to stand in its place; but not so with clothing, because kiswah (with kasrah) means clothing, so it is necessary that...
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute explaining the Hanafi position versus the Shafi'i school on the method of feeding in expiation (kafarah). The text begins by clarifying that giving one person the amount for two months in one day is only valid for that one day, but giving sixty separate poor people in one day is valid regardless. It then states the Hanafi position: both ibahah (making food available) and tamleek (transferring ownership) are permissible. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i requires tamleek exclusively, drawing an analogy with clothing (kiswah) where ownership transfer is mandatory. The Hanafi proof comes from the principle of dalalat al-nass (indication of the text) in Usul al-Fiqh. The Quranic phrase 'feeding ten poor people' (Quran 5:89) linguistically means making them ta'im (one who eats), which is achieved by ibahah (making food available). Tamleek is only included by implication (dalala) because the overall objective is fulfilling the needy's needs, and tamleek can serve that purpose more effectively in many cases, so it is annexed to ibahah. However, in clothing, the word kiswah (garment) necessarily implies ownership transfer, so ibahah is insufficient. The commentary also explains that the root meaning of it'am is to make someone eat, not to make them own.

Key Terms
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): A principle in Usul al-Fiqh where the wording of the text indicates a ruling beyond its literal meaning, based on the underlying purpose.
طاعم (ta'im): One who eats or tastes food; the active participle of ta'ima (to eat).
إباحة (ibahah): Making something permissible or available for use, without transfer of ownership.
تمليك (tamleek): Transfer of ownership, making someone the owner of an item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi argument for allowing ibahah (making food available) in feeding kafarah?
A) The verse uses the word 'kiswah' which implies ibahah
B) The word 'it'am' linguistically means making someone a ta'im (eater), which is achieved by ibahah
C) There is a consensus among all schools that ibahah suffices
D) The verse specifies that ownership must be transferred

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that feeding (it'am) in kafarah is fulfilled by making the poor eat (ibahah), and tamleek (ownership) is only needed by implication, not as a requirement.
