Emancipation through Ownership of a Mahram Relative
Explaining the rule that owning a mahram relative leads to automatic emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on emancipation through ownership of a mahram relative and identify the scope of its application (owner capacity, type of ownership, and partial ownership).

Core Idea
A mahram relative becomes free automatically upon ownership, regardless of owner's capacity or consent.

This passage explains a key Hanafi ruling: if a person comes to own a relative who is a mahram (with whom marriage is permanently prohibited), that relative is immediately emancipated. This rule, based on a hadith, applies even if the owner is a minor, insane, or non-Muslim, and whether ownership is voluntary (purchase, gift) or involuntary (inheritance). In this lesson, we will unpack the ruling, its evidence, and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage to determine the precise ruling: a mahram relative becomes free upon ownership. Note that the ruling is general, covering all types of ownership and all owners regardless of legal capacity.
The ruling is established by a hadith and is not contingent on the owner's intention.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The passage cites the hadith: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, then he is free.' Identify the source and the transmission level (narrated by the four Sunan, ahad but clear in meaning).
The hadith is the sole basis for the ruling, and its wording is explicit.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The phrase 'فهو حر' is a declarative statement that implies immediate emancipation. In Hanafi usul, such explicit statements are binding. The ruling is not subject to istihsan.
The hadith's clarity (dalalah qat'iyyah) outweighs any potential objection based on owner incompetence.
4
Analyze the implications: owner capacity and ownership types
The passage explicitly states that the ruling applies even if the owner is a child, insane, or disbeliever. It also covers voluntary and involuntary ownership, and partial ownership (half becomes free).
This is based on the slave's right to freedom, analogous to the obligation to support a relative.
5
Note cross-madhhab nuance
While the Hanafi school applies the ruling universally, some other schools may restrict it to competent owners or Muslims. This difference does not affect the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The passage does not detail the opposing views but implies acceptance of the universal application.

It cannot be said: How can it be effective on a child and an insane person while they are not among the people qualified for emancipation? And in the generality of 'ownership' there is an indication that the ruling includes voluntary ownership like ownership by purchase or acceptance of gift, and involuntary like inheritance, and also that if he owns half of him, that half becomes free upon him. The basis for all this is the hadith: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, then he is free' narrated by the authors of the four Sunan, and in a narration of al-Nasa'i: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free upon him.'

Commentary
This passage explains that owning a mahram relative (e.g., one's own father, mother, child, sibling) automatically results in the emancipation of that relative. This ruling applies even if the owner is not legally competent (a child, insane person, or non-Muslim) because the slave has a right to freedom. The emancipation is effective immediately upon ownership, regardless of how ownership was acquired (purchase, gift, inheritance). If one owns only half of the relative, that half becomes free. The primary evidence is the prophetic hadith narrated by multiple sources.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A relative who is a mahram, meaning one with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (e.g., parent, child, sibling).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Emancipation: Valid Despite Motive or State
Ruling on emancipation regardless of motive or state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of emancipation when done for an idol, under duress, or while intoxicated, and explain the rationale for its validity despite motives or state.

Core Idea
Emancipation is a unilateral act that takes effect regardless of motive or the agent's state — only the physical utterance matters.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi ruling: that emancipation remains valid even if the person performing it does so for an idol, under compulsion, or while drunk. While these situations may seem to invalidate ordinary transactions, the commentators explain that emancipation is a unilateral iqaa that does not require intention or consent. Understanding this principle clarifies why the slave becomes free in all these cases, even if the agent's motives lead to other consequences like disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their motives
The passage covers four scenarios: emancipation for Allah's sake, for an idol, under duress, and while drunk. Identify each scenario and what the agent is doing.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
According to the Hanafi school, all four types result in a valid emancipation. The slave is freed immediately upon utterance.
3
Understand the rationale
Emancipation is a unilateral act (iqaa). Its validity depends only on the proper utterance by a qualified person. Intention and consent are not required, unlike bilateral contracts.
This is based on talil (legal reasoning) that the act itself is sufficient.
4
Note the consequence of intention for worship
If emancipation is done for an idol with the intention of veneration, the person commits kufr. However, the emancipation still takes effect.
The legal effect (freeing the slave) is separate from the creedal consequence.
5
Compare with other schools
Other madhhabs (e.g., Shafi'i) may invalidate the drunk's emancipation due to lack of mental capacity. Hanafis consider it valid because the utterance alone suffices.
This ikhtilaf is based on different views of intention in unilateral acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أو أعتق لوجه الله ؛ أي لذاته أو رضاه.
[٢] قوله : أو للصنم ؛ الصَّنَمُ . بفتحتين . صورة الإنسان من خشب أو ذهب أو فضة، فلو من حجر فهو وثن. كذا في «البحر » ) ، والمراد به هاهنا ما يعم الوثن وغيره، ويكفر في صورة الإعتاق للصنمِ وللشيطان إن قصد تعظيمه والتقرب إليه. كذا في «الجوهرة النيرة».
[۳] قوله : أو مكرهاً ؛ - بفتح الراء - ، اسم مفعول من الإكراه ؛ أي حال كونه مكرهاً، و كذلك السكران.
His statement: 'or he emancipated for the sake of Allah' meaning for His essence or His pleasure. [2] His statement: 'or for the idol'; al-sanam, with two fatha, is a human figure made of wood, gold, or silver; if from stone it is wathan. As in al-Bahr. And what is meant here is general, including wathan and others. And he becomes a disbeliever in the case of emancipating for the idol or for Satan if he intended veneration and seeking nearness. As in al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah. [3] His statement: 'or under compulsion' - with fatha on the ra - is a passive participle from ikrah, meaning in a state of being coerced, and similarly the drunken one.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage explains that the validity of emancipation is not affected by the motive or the state of the person performing it. If someone emancipates a slave for the sake of Allah (seeking His pleasure), it is valid. If they emancipate for an idol or Satan, the emancipation is still valid (because it is an act from a qualified person in its proper place), but if they intended worship of that entity, they commit disbelief (kufr). Similarly, if a person is coerced (mukrah) or drunk (sakran) and performs emancipation, it is valid because the act of emancipation itself is effective regardless of the state of the person, provided the physical action occurred.

Key Terms
الصنم (al-sanam): An idol made in the form of a human from wood, gold, or silver; if from stone it is called wathan. In this context, it refers generally to any object of worship besides Allah.
المكره (al-mukrah): A person who is coerced or forced to do something against his will.
السكران (al-sakran): A person intoxicated to the point of losing mental control. His utterances are still considered valid for emancipation but not for contracts like sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is valid and effective.
C) It is valid only if the drunk was forced to drink.
D) It becomes valid after the person sobers up and confirms.

Key Takeaway
Emancipation is a powerful verbal act that once spoken, takes effect regardless of motive, duress, or intoxication, unless the utterance itself is impossible.

Effectiveness of Manumission Despite Intention or Coercion
Ruling with proof on manumission in six scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that manumission is effective in all listed circumstances and support it with the relevant hadith and analogy.

Core Idea
Manumission is a binding act that takes effect even when done sinfully, jestingly, under duress, or while drunk.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle: the validity of manumission does not depend on the intention of the owner or the presence of free will. The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya lists six scenarios where manumission occurs and provides proofs from hadith and analogy. Understanding this principle reveals the school's emphasis on the effective cause (illah) of the act rather than the subjective state of the agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
List the six scenarios where manumission is ruled effective: ownership of a mahram, freeing for Allah, for the devil, for an idol, under coercion, and while drunk.
Each scenario tests a different potential obstacle: intention, belief, duress, or intoxication.
2
Examine the proofs for each scenario
For the mahram case, the hadith is cited. For devil/idol, analogy to divorce is used. For coercion and drunkenness, the hadith about three serious matters (divorce, marriage, manumission) applies.
Note that the hadith chain for the three matters is weak, but the ruling is accepted by the school.
3
Analyse the common legal principle
The underlying principle is that manumission (like divorce) is a legal act whose effectiveness is not contingent on religious acceptance or personal intention. The act issues from a competent person in a valid context.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i where intention may be required for validity.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Shafi'i school, freeing for an idol or under coercion may be invalid. In Hanafi, it is valid, though the latter incurs sin.
This affects cases of doubt about the validity of past manumissions, e.g., in inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق ألفاظه
ذا رحم محرم منه، أو أعتق لوجه الله تعالى، أو للشيطان، أو للصنم، أو مكرهاً، أو سكران
ذا رحم محرم منه، أو أعتق لوجه الله تعالى، أو للشيطان، أو للصنم، أو مكرهاً، أو سكران
الإعتاق؛ لأنّا نقول: هذا العتق تعلق به حق العبد، فشابه نفقة القريب. كذا في «الهداية».
وفي إطلاق الملك إشارة إلى أنّ الحكم شامل للملك الاختياري كالملك بالشراء، وقبول الهبة، والاضطراري كالإرث، وإلى أنه لو ملك نصفه عُتِق عليه ذلك النصف. والأصل في هذا كله حديث: «من ملك ذا رحم محرم منه فهو حر» أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة، وفي رواية للنسائي: «من ملك ذا رحم محرم منه عتق عليه». قوله: أو أعتق لوجه الله؛ أي لذاته أو رضاه.
[٢] قوله: أو للصنم؛ الصَّنَمُ بفتحتين صورة الإنسان من خشب أو ذهب أو فضة، فلو من حجر فهو وثن. كذا في «البحر»، والمراد به هاهنا ما يعم الوثن وغيره، ويكفر في صورة الإعتاق للصنم وللشيطان إن قصد تعظيمه والتقرب إليه. كذا في «الجوهرة النيرة».
[۳] قوله: أو مكرهاً؛ - بفتح الراء -، اسم مفعول من الإكراه؛ أي حال كونه مكرهاً، أكرهه إنسان سواء كان عبده أو غيره على الإعتاق، سواء كان الإكراه ملجأ: وهو ما يخاف به فوت النفس أو العضو أو غير ملجئ: وهو ما بخلافه.
[١]قوله: إلى ملك، وكذا لو أضافه إلى سببه، نحو: إن اشتريت عبداً فهو حرّ.
[٢]قوله: عتق؛ أي ذلك العبد عليه، أما عتقه في صورة ملك ذي رحم محرم فلما مرَّ من الحديث، والوجه فيه: هو صلة الرحم. وأما العتق في صورة الإعتاق لوجه الله، فلأن العتق عبارة يثاب عليها كما مر، والعبادة لا تكون إلا لوجه الله، فالتصريح به يؤكده.
وأما في صورة الإعتاق للشيطان والصنم؛ فلأنّ نفس التصرُّف صدر من أهله في محله، فلا يتوقف نفاذه على قصد القربة، وحرمة تصرّفه شرعاً لا تنافي عدم ترتب أثره ونفاذه، كما إذا طلّق زوجته ثلاث تطليقات في مجلس واحد، تقع ويأثم.
وأما في صورة الإكراه والسكر فلان العتاق كالطلاق يقع بالهزل؛ لحديث: «ثلاث جدهن جد، وهزلهن جد الطلاق، والنكاح والعتاق»، وأخرجه الطبراني بلفظ: «ثلاث لا يجوز اللعب فيهن الطلاق، والنكاح والعتق»، وفي رواية الحارث ابن أبي أسامة في مسنده: «لا يجوز اللعب في ثلاث الطلاق والنكاح والعتاق، فمن قالهن فقد وجبن». وعند عبد الرزاق في مصنفه: «مَن طلّق وهو لاعب فطلاقه جائز، ومن أعتق وهو لاعب فعتاقه جائز، ومَن نكح وهو لاعب فنكاحه جائز»، وأخرج عبد الرزاق نحوه موقوفاً على عمر و عليه ، و في أسانيد هذه الروايات ضعف، كما بسط الحافظ
Book of Manumission: Its wordings. A mahram relative [is freed if owned], or if he freed for the sake of Allah, or for the devil, or for the idol, or while coerced, or while drunk. A mahram relative [is freed if owned], or if he freed for the sake of Allah, or for the devil, or for the idol, or while coerced, or while drunk. Manumission [is effective], because we say: This emancipation involves the right of the slave, so it resembles the maintenance of a relative. As in al-Hidayah. And the unqualified mention of ownership indicates that the ruling includes optional ownership like ownership by purchase and accepting a gift, and compulsory ownership like inheritance, and that if one owns half of him, that half is freed. The basis for all this is the hadith: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free' narrated by the authors of the four Sunan, and in a narration of al-Nasa'i: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he is freed by that ownership.' His statement: 'or freed for the sake of Allah' means for His essence or His pleasure. [2] His statement: 'or for the idol' – al-ṣanam (with two fathas) is a human figure of wood, gold, or silver; if of stone, it is wathan. As in al-Bahr, and the intended meaning here is what includes idol and other. One becomes a disbeliever in the case of freeing for the idol or for the devil if he intends veneration and seeking proximity. As in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. [3] His statement: 'or while coerced' – with fatḥa on the rā', passive participle from coercion, meaning being coerced, a person coerced him whether his slave or someone else into manumitting, whether the coercion is mulji' (what fears loss of life or limb) or non-mulji' (otherwise). [1] His statement: 'to ownership' – and similarly if he added it to its cause, like: 'If I buy a slave, he is free.' [2] His statement: 'he is freed' – meaning that slave becomes free by him. As for his freedom in the case of owning a mahram relative, due to the hadith mentioned, and the reason is maintaining family ties. As for the manumission in the case of freeing for the sake of Allah, because manumission is an act for which reward is given, as has passed, and worship is only for the sake of Allah, so explicitly stating it emphasizes it. As for the case of freeing for the devil and the idol, because the action itself is issued by a person who is eligible for it in the proper place, so its enforcement does not depend on the intention of devotion, and the prohibition of his action religiously does not preclude the existence of its effect and enforcement, just as if he divorces his wife three divorces in one sitting, they occur and he sins. As for the case of coercion and drunkenness, because manumission is like divorce – it takes effect even in jest, due to the hadith: 'Three things whose seriousness is serious and whose jest is serious: divorce, marriage, and manumission.' Al-Tabarani narrated with the wording: 'Three things in which jest is not allowed: divorce, marriage, and manumission.' In a narration of al-Harith ibn Abi Usama in his Musnad: 'Jest is not allowed in three things: divorce, marriage, and manumission. Whoever says them, they become binding.' And according to 'Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf: 'Whoever divorces while joking, his divorce is valid; whoever frees while joking, his manumission is valid; whoever marries while joking, his marriage is valid.' And 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated similar as a mawquf hadith from 'Umar. And in the chains of these narrations there is weakness, as al-Hafiz has elaborated.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the effectiveness of manumission in various circumstances. The author from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya comments on the matn of al-Wiqaya, listing cases where manumission is effective: owning a mahram relative, freeing for Allah's sake, for the devil, for an idol, under coercion, or while drunk. The commentary explains each case.

First, if a person owns a mahram relative (e.g., brother, uncle, etc.), that slave becomes free immediately. This is derived from the hadith: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free.' The reason given is maintaining family ties (sila al-rahim). The text notes that this applies whether ownership is voluntary (purchase, gift) or compulsory (inheritance), and it applies even to partial ownership.

Second, freeing for the sake of Allah is effective because manumission is a praiseworthy act of worship, and explicitly stating the intention confirms it.

Third, freeing for the devil or an idol is still effective as a legal manumission, even though the doer commits disbelief if he intends veneration. The action itself is from a competent person in a valid context, so it takes effect despite the sinful intention. Analogous to divorce: if a man divorces his wife three times in one sitting, the divorce occurs and he sins.

Fourth, under coercion (ikrah), whether severe (fear of death or limb loss) or mild, the manumission is effective. The coerced person is still considered to have uttered the words, and the act is not nullified by duress.

Fifth, a drunken person's manumission is effective. The ruling is based on the hadith: 'Three things whose seriousness is serious and whose jest is serious: divorce, marriage, and manumission.' These are serious contracts that take effect regardless of playful intent. The hadith is cited with multiple narrations, noting that some chains are weak, but the ruling is established.

In summary, manumission is a binding legal act that does not require a specific intention or voluntary consent to be valid, similar to marriage and divorce.

Key Terms
رحم محرم (rahm mahram): A relative who is prohibited for marriage due to consanguinity (e.g., brother, uncle).
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion by another person to force an action, whether severe (fear of life or limb) or not.
صنم (sanam): An idol made of wood, gold, or silver in human form; stone idols are 'wathan'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a circumstance in which manumission is effective according to the text?
A) Owning a mahram relative
B) Freeing for the sake of the devil
C) Freeing while under the influence of a sleeping pill
D) Freeing under coercion

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, manumission is a binding legal act that takes effect regardless of the owner's intention, sobriety, or freedom from coercion.

The Binding Nature of Emancipation: Proofs from Hadith and Hanafi Ruling
Commentary on categories and proofs of valid emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of emancipation under coercion, jest, and intoxication, and identify the dalil (hadith) that supports this position.

Core Idea
The utterance of emancipation is binding regardless of intention—even in jest, coercion, or intoxication.

In this passage, the commentator on Al-Wiqayah explains the categories of valid emancipation in the Hanafi school. The key proof is a hadith stating that three matters—divorce, marriage, and emancipation—are binding even when done in jest. The Hanafi jurists use this to argue that since jest (which lacks any intention) is valid, then coercion (where intention exists) is even more worthy of validity. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of valid emancipation
From the commentary, list the scenarios under which emancipation is considered valid: owning a blood relative (mahram), for the sake of Allah, for the devil/idol, under coercion, in jest, and while intoxicated. Also note emancipation added to a cause or condition.
The commentator also distinguishes between blood relatives who are mahram and those who are not, and between mahram by blood and other prohibited relations.
2
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith quoted: 'ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: الطلاق والنكاح والعتاق' (Three things are serious and their jest is serious: divorce, marriage, and emancipation). Note that it is reported through multiple chains, some weak but collectively strong.
The commentator cites additional narrations from al-Tabarani, al-Harith ibn Abi Usama, and Abd al-Razzaq, including a saying of Umar (ra).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly states that these three actions are binding even in jest. This indicates that the mere utterance suffices for legal effect; intention is not a necessary condition.
The Hanafi school takes this as a general principle: the outward action (lafdh) is sufficient for these three matters.
4
Apply the a fortiori argument (qiyas awlawi)
Since jest (which lacks any intention) results in valid emancipation, then coercion (where the person has intention, albeit compelled) is even more appropriate to be valid. Similarly, intoxication is included as a deterrent.
The passage explicitly says: 'فلان يقع بالإكراه أولى' (then it is more appropriate under coercion). This is an argument from the lesser to the greater.

He said: 'a relative by blood, coerced' – a person coerces him, whether it is his own slave or someone else, to emancipate, whether the coercion is pressing (which fears loss of life or limb) or non-pressing (otherwise). [1] He said: 'to ownership' and likewise if he adds it to its cause, like: if I buy a slave, he is free. [2] He said: 'he becomes free' i.e. that slave upon him. As for his emancipation in the case of owning a blood relative (mahram), it is due to the hadith that passed, and the reason is maintaining kinship. As for emancipation for the sake of Allah, because emancipation is an act that rewards as mentioned, and worship is only for Allah, so stating it emphasizes. As for emancipation for the devil or idol, because the action itself comes from its rightful doer in its proper place, so its validity does not depend on intention of piety, and the prohibition of the action does not negate its effect and validity, just as if he divorces his wife three times in one sitting, it takes effect and he sins. As for coercion and intoxication, because emancipation like divorce takes effect with jest, due to the hadith: 'Three things are serious and their jest is serious: divorce, marriage, and emancipation'. And reported by Tabarani with wording: 'Three things are not to be played with: divorce, marriage, and emancipation'. And in a narration of al-Harith ibn Abi Usama in his Musnad: 'Play is not allowed in three: divorce, marriage, and emancipation, so whoever says them, they become binding'. And according to Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf: 'Whoever divorces while playing, his divorce is valid; whoever emancipates while playing, his emancipation is valid; and whoever marries while playing, his marriage is valid'. And Abd al-Razzaq narrated similarly as a saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). The chains of these narrations are weak, as al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar detailed in Talkhis al-Habir, but it is compensated by the multiplicity of chains. Since the occurrence of emancipation in jest is established, even though the jester has no intention at all, then its occurrence under coercion is more appropriate, because the coerced person has intention, though it is due to coercion. And the intoxicated person's emancipation and divorce occur as a deterrent. And what is appropriate for this discussion has passed in the discussion of divorce. The Book of Emancipation: Its Phrasing Meaning: a relative by blood due to the womb. And his saying: 'mahram' is an adjective of 'dha', and its being in the genitive is due to adjacency. And his saying: 'to ownership' like: if I own a slave, he is free. Or 'condition' and it is found like: if so-and-so arrives, my slave is free, then the condition is found, he becomes free. [1] He said: meaning a relative by blood due to the womb; he indicates by this that the womb originally is the vessel of the fetus inside his mother, then the kinship resulting from it is called by it, and he excludes by it the mahram who is not a blood relative, like the wife of his father, the wife of his son, the mother of his wife, and foster sisters, etc. [2] He said: 'mahram'; he excludes by it the blood relative who is not mahram like the children of paternal and maternal uncles and aunts. (3) He said: 'and its being in the genitive' is a rebuttal to what is said: if it were an adjective of 'dha rahim', it would be accusative not genitive. The rebuttal is that the genitive here is due to adjacency, i.e., connection with the adjacent word, and consideration of harmony, and this occurs frequently in Arabic speech. From it is His saying: 'and wipe your heads and your feet to the ankles' (Quran 5:6) with the kasra of the lam of 'arjulakum', and from it is His saying: 'Indeed I fear for you the punishment of a Day' (Quran 11:26) with the kasra of the mim, while it is an adjective of the possessed noun due to adjacency to the genitive 'day'. [4] He said: 'like: if I own...etc.'; he indicates by this that what is meant by 'adding' in the matn is conditioning, and its equivalent is adding divorce to ownership or condition, and its discussion has passed in its place. [0] He said: 'or condition and it is found'; its apparent meaning indicates that the author's phrase 'and it is found' is connected to his saying 'or condition', and its pronoun refers back to it. But the better is what we indicated previously: that it is connected to both condition and ownership, and its pronoun refers back to both.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqayah, discussing various scenarios in which emancipation (عتاق) is valid and effective in the Hanafi school. The commentator explains that emancipation takes effect in three main categories: (1) when a person owns a blood relative (dhu rahim mahram), (2) when emancipation is added to the cause of ownership (e.g., 'if I buy a slave, he is free'), and (3) when it is conditioned on a future event (e.g., 'if so-and-so arrives, my slave is free'). Additionally, the commentator addresses situations where the emancipator is coerced, jesting, or intoxicated, ruling that the emancipation is still valid. The proof is a hadith stating that three things—divorce, marriage, and emancipation—are serious and binding even when done in jest. The commentator argues that if jest (which lacks any intention) makes emancipation binding, then coercion (where intention is present, albeit compelled) is even more deserving of validity. Intoxicated emancipation is also valid as a deterrent. The passage also clarifies the grammatical point that the word 'mahram' in the matn is in the genitive case due to adjacency to 'dha rahim', not because it is a descriptive adjective. The commentator excludes from the category of 'dhu rahim mahram' those who are prohibited in marriage but not related by blood (e.g., step-relations, in-laws, foster relatives) and blood relatives who are not mahram (e.g., cousins). The entire discussion affirms the Hanafi principle that the outward utterance of emancipation is sufficient for its validity; intention is not a necessary condition.

Key Terms
عتاق ('itaq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing a slave.
ذا رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A blood relative within prohibited degrees of marriage (e.g., mother, sister, daughter).
الجر بالجوار (al-jarr bil-jiwar): A grammatical phenomenon where a word is placed in the genitive case due to its adjacency to another word that is genitive, even though it would normally be in a different case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on emancipation performed under coercion (ikrah)?
A) It is invalid because the person did not intend it.
B) It is valid but the person is sinful.
C) It is valid and the slave becomes free.
D) It is suspended until the coerced person confirms it after the coercion ends.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, emancipation is valid by mere utterance, even without intention, as proven by the hadith that divorce, marriage, and emancipation are binding in jest.

Child Follows Mother in Legal Status: Rule, Proof, and Distinctions
Establishes rule of maternal followership with proof and key distinctions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a child's legal status follows the mother, explain the proof (ijma and rational reasoning), distinguish between slavery (riqq) and ownership (milk), and identify key exceptions like the child of the deceived (maghrur).

Core Idea
A child's legal status follows the mother, not the father—based on consensus and fetal unity.

In Hanafi law, the child is not independent but derives its legal status from the mother. This lesson unpacks the foundational rule that a child follows the mother in ownership, slavery, and emancipation. We will examine the proof from consensus (ijma) and rational arguments, the critical distinction between slavery (riqq) and ownership (milk), and important exceptions such as the child of a deceived husband.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The rule is that a child follows its mother in ownership, slavery, freedom, tadbir, istilad, and kitabah. This applies to the fetus while still attached to the mother.
The child is not free simply because the father is free.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites consensus (ijma) of the Ummah from al-Kanz. It also provides rational arguments: the child's water is consumed by the mother's, lineage is certain through her, and the fetus is like a limb of the mother physically and legally.
Consensus is a qati' (definitive) source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The explicit statement of consensus directly establishes the rule. Rational arguments reinforce that the mother's side is preponderant, making her status dominant.
The rule is wajib, not fard, because it derives from consensus and reason, not a direct Quranic command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
The Shafi'i school holds that if the father is free, the child is free. The Hanafi school rejects this, maintaining that the child follows the mother regardless, except in the maghrur case.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preponderance)
The Hanafi position is upheld due to stronger proofs (consensus, rational unity) and is the relied-upon view in the madhhab.
The text also clarifies that there is no repetition: earlier discussion was about emancipation of the fetus as a principal, this is about following as a secondary matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتاق الفاظه
والولد يتبع أمه في الملك، والرق، والعتق وفروعه
والولد يتبع أمه في الملك ، والرِّق، والعتق وفروعه) : أي إن كانت الأم في ملك زيد، فالولد المولود في ملك زيد يكون ملكاً له
[1] قوله : والولد ؛ المراد به الجنين المتصل بالأم، فإنه لو ولدت ولداً ثم أَعْتَقَ مولى الأم الأم لا يعتق هو تبعاً. كذا في «البحر».
[۲] قوله : يتبع أمه ؛ قال في «كشف الوقاية»: «قال في «الكنز»: الولد يتبع الأم في الملك والحرية والرق والتدبير والاستيلاد والكتابة بإجماع الأمة، وقال في شرحه «التبيين»: «لأن ماءه يكون مستهلكاً بمائها، فيرجح جانبها، ولأنه تيقن به من جهتها ؛ ولهذا يثبت نسب ولد الزنا وولد الملاعنة منها حتى ترثه ويرثها، ولأنه قبل الانفصال هو كعضو من أعضائها حسّاً وحكماً ، حتى يتغذى بغذائها ، وينتقل بانتقالها، ويدخل في البيع والعتق وغيرهما من التصرفات تبعاً لها.
فكان جانبها أرجح، ولذلك يعتبر جانب الأم في البهائم أيضاً، حتى إذا تولّد بين الوحشي والأهلي ؛ أو بين المأكول وغير المأكول يؤكل إن كانت أمه مأكولة، ويجوز الأضحية به إن كانت أمه مما تجوز الأضحية به.
فحاصله : إنّ الولد يتبع أمه فيما ذكرنا ، والأب في النسب ؛ لأنه للتعريف ، والأم لا تُشْهر.
والفرق بين الرق والملكِ أنّ الرقّ : هو الذلّ الذي يركبه الله على عباده جزاء استنكافهم عن طاعته، وهو حق الله أو حق العامة على ما اختلفوا فيه. والملك : هو تمكن الشخص من التصرف فيه، وهو حقه، وأول ما يؤخذ المأسور يوصف بالرق، ولا يوصفُ بالملك إلا بعد الإخراج إلى دار الإسلام. والملك يوجد في الحيوان والجماد، والحيوان غير الآدمي دون الرق، وبالبيع يزول ملكه دون الرق، وبالعتق يزولُ ملكه قصداً لأنه حقه، ويزول الرق ضمناً ضرورةً فراغه عن حقوق العباد.
ويتبين لك الفرق بينهما في القنّ وأمّ الولد والمكاتب، فإنّ الرق والملك كاملان في القن، ورق أمّ الولد ناقص، حتى لا يجوز عتقها عن كفارة، والملك فيها كامل والمكاتب رقه كامل، حتى جاز عتقه عن الكفّارة، وملكه ناقص حتى خرج من يد
وولد الأمة من زوجها ملك لسيّدِها، وولدها من مولاها حرّ وإن كانت الأم مشتركة كان الولد مشتركاً على سهام الأم، وإن كانت مرقوقة ، فالولد المولود حال رقيتها يكون مرقوقاً ، وكذا يتبعها في العتق وفروعه : كالكتابة ، والتدبير، فعتق الولد بتبعيَّةِ الأُمِّ إنّما يكونُ إذا كان بين العتق والولادة ستة أشهر أو أكثر ، فحينئذ ينجر الولاء إلى موالي الأب، فعلم أنه لا تكرار .
(وولد الأمة من زوجها ملك لسيّدها ) ، وولدها من مولاها حرّ) (1) المولى، ولا يدخل تحت قوله : كل مملوك لي حر). انتهى. 11 ] قوله : مشتركة ؛ أي بين اثنين فأكثر، فالولد المولود من تلك الجارية يكون مشتركاً على قدر حصصهم في الأم. [٢] قوله : مرقوقة ؛ سواء كانت مملوكة أو لا، فإنّ بين الملك والرق عموماً وخصوصاً من وجه على ما مرّ سابقاً غير مرة، خلافاً لما ذكره الشارح له سابقاً من أنه لا يكون مرقوقاً إلا بأن يكون مملوكاً.
(۳) قوله : في العتق ...الخ ؛ فإذا أعتق المولى الجارية عتق ولدها تبعاً لها، وكذا إذا دبرت صار مدبّراً، وكذا إذا كوتبت دخلَ في كتابتها، وهذا كله تبعاً لا أصالة. [٤] قوله : فعلم أنه لا تكرار ؛ دفع لما يرد على المصنف له أنه قد ذكر عتق الحمل بعتق الأم سابقاً ، ثم ذكر تبعية الولد للأم في الرق فهو تكرار، وحاصل الدفع أن الحكم السابق كان في عتق الحمل أصالة، وهذا في عتقه تبعاً فلا تكرار، وقد مر سابقاً وجه الفرق بينهما.
[0] قوله : ملك لسيدها ؛ لما مرّ من أنّ الولد يتبع الأم في الرق والملك، فلا يكون حراً، وإن كان أبوه حرّاً، ويستثنى منه ولد المغرور ؛ فإنّه حرّ بالقيمة، كان يتزوج الحر امرأة على أنها حرّة ، فإذا هي قنة، فأولاده منها أحراراً بالقيمة، وقد يكون الولد حراً من رقيقين بلا تحرير ، كأن نكح عبد أمة أبيه فولده حرّ ؛ لأنه ولد ولد المولى. كذا في «الظهيرية».
[٦] قوله : حرّ ؛ لأنه مخلوق من مائه فيعتق عليه. كذا في «الهداية» (٢).
Book of Emancipation, its expressions. The child follows its mother in ownership, slavery, emancipation and its branches. That is: if the mother is in the ownership of Zayd, then the child born in the ownership of Zayd becomes his property. [1] His statement: 'the child' – what is meant is the fetus attached to the mother, because if she gave birth to a child and then the master of the mother emancipated the mother, the child is not emancipated as a follower. Likewise in 'al-Bahr'. [2] His statement: 'follows its mother' – he said in 'Kashf al-Wiqayah': 'He said in 'al-Kanz': The child follows the mother in ownership, freedom, slavery, tadbir, istilad, and kitabah by consensus of the Ummah.' And he said in its commentary 'al-Tabyin': 'Because his water is consumed by her water, so her side is preponderant, and because his lineage is confirmed through her; for this reason the lineage of the child of zina and the child of li'an is established from her such that she inherits from him and he inherits from her, and because before separation he is like a limb of her limbs physically and legally, such that he is nourished by her nourishment, moves with her movement, and enters into sale, emancipation, and other transactions as a follower of her. So her side is more preponderant; therefore the mother's side is considered even in animals, such that if a hybrid is born between a wild and domestic animal, or between edible and non-edible, it is eaten if its mother is edible, and it is permissible to sacrifice it if its mother is of a type permissible for sacrifice. So the summary: the child follows its mother in what we have mentioned, and the father in lineage, because lineage is for identification, and the mother is not well-known (for lineage). And the difference between slavery (riqq) and ownership (milk) is that slavery is the humiliation that Allah imposes on His servants as a punishment for their refusal to obey Him, and it is the right of Allah or the right of the public, according to differing opinions. Ownership is the person's ability to dispose of something, and it is his right. The captive is first described as being in slavery, and is not described as being owned except after being brought to the abode of Islam. Ownership exists in animals and inanimate objects, and in non-human animals without slavery. By sale, ownership is removed but not slavery; by emancipation, ownership is removed intentionally because it is his right, and slavery is removed implicitly out of necessity due to its being emptied of the rights of people. And the difference between them becomes clear in the cases of the full slave (qinn), the umm walad, and the mukatab. For the full slave, both slavery and ownership are complete. The slavery of the umm walad is deficient, such that it is not permissible to emancipate her for expiation, but her ownership is complete. The mukatab has complete slavery, such that his emancipation is permissible for expiation, but his ownership is deficient, such that he leaves his hand... And the child of a slave woman from her husband is the property of her master; and her child from her master is free. And if the mother is co-owned, the child is co-owned according to the shares of the mother. And if she is enslaved (marquqah), the child born during her enslavement is enslaved. Likewise the child follows her in emancipation and its branches: like kitabah and tadbir. So the emancipation of the child by following the mother only occurs if between the emancipation and the birth there are six months or more; then the wala' is drawn to the father's masters. So it is known that there is no repetition. And the child of a slave woman from her husband is the property of her master; and her child from her master is free – the master, and does not enter under his statement: 'Every slave of mine is free.' End. [11] His statement: 'co-owned' – i.e., between two or more, so the child born from that slave girl is co-owned according to the proportion of their shares in the mother. [2] His statement: 'enslaved' – whether she is owned or not, because between ownership and slavery there is a general and specific relationship in one sense, as has passed many times, contrary to what the commentator mentioned earlier that she would not be enslaved unless she is owned. (3) His statement: 'in emancipation... etc.' – so when the master emancipates the slave girl, her child is emancipated as a follower of her; likewise if she is made mudabbarah, he becomes mudabbar; likewise if she enters kitabah, he enters into her kitabah. All of this is as a follower, not as a principal. [4] His statement: 'so it is known that there is no repetition' – a rebuttal to the objection against the author that he had mentioned the emancipation of the fetus by the emancipation of the mother earlier, and then mentioned the following of the child to the mother in slavery – that is repetition. The summary of the rebuttal is that the previous ruling was regarding the emancipation of the fetus as a principal, and this is regarding his emancipation as a follower, so there is no repetition. The distinction between them has passed earlier. [0] His statement: 'property of her master' – because of what has passed that the child follows the mother in slavery and ownership, so he is not free, even if his father is free. An exception is the child of the deceived (al-maghrur): he is free with payment of value. For example, a free man marries a woman thinking she is free, but she turns out to be a slave girl, then his children from her are free with payment of value. And sometimes a child can be free from two slaves without manumission, as when a slave marries his master's slave woman, then his child is free because he is the child of the master's child. Likewise in 'al-Zahiriyyah'. [6] His statement: 'free' – because he is created from his (the master's) water, so he is emancipated upon him. Likewise in 'al-Hidayah'.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi rule that a child follows its mother in matters of legal status: ownership, slavery, freedom, and related branches like tadbir, istilad, and kitabah. The commentator begins by clarifying that 'child' here refers to the fetus still attached to the mother; if the mother is emancipated after birth, the already-born child does not automatically become free. The proof for this rule is given as consensus (ijma) of the Ummah, and rational arguments: the child's essence is consumed by the mother's, her side is preponderant, lineage is certain through her, and physically and legally the fetus is like a limb of the mother. This reasoning extends even to animals: the edibility of a hybrid follows the mother. A key distinction is made between slavery (riqq) and ownership (milk): slavery is a divinely imposed humiliation and a right of Allah (or the public), while ownership is the right of the individual to dispose. Examples illustrate the difference: a full slave (qinn) has both complete; an umm walad has deficient slavery (cannot be used for expiation) but complete ownership; a mukatab has complete slavery but deficient ownership (cannot dispose freely). The passage then states that a child of a slave woman from her husband belongs to the mother's master, but a child from her master (impregnated by him) is free because it is created from his water. If the mother is co-owned, the child is co-owned proportionally. For the child to be emancipated by following the mother's emancipation, there must be at least six months between the emancipation and birth; then the wala' goes to the father's masters. The commentator also clarifies that there is no repetition in the text because the earlier ruling was about the fetus being emancipatated as a principal (when the mother is emancipated while pregnant), while this ruling is about the child following as a secondary matter. Exceptions are noted: the child of a deceived (maghrur) is free with payment of value, and in some cases a child can be free from two slaves without manumission.

Key Terms
رق (riqq): Slavery, a legal status of humiliation imposed by Allah as punishment, considered a right of Allah or the public.
ملك (milk): Ownership, the ability to dispose of something as one's right, applicable to both animate and inanimate objects.
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Following or derivative status, where a child acquires the legal status of the mother as a dependent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a slave woman gives birth to a child from her free husband, what is the legal status of the child?
A) The child is free because the father is free.
B) The child is a slave belonging to the mother's master.
C) The child is free because it follows the father's status.
D) The child is a slave only if the mother is a full slave (qinn).

Key Takeaway
The child's legal status in matters of ownership, slavery, and emancipation is determined by the mother, based on consensus and the physical-legal unity of mother and child.

Ruling on the Child of a Slave Woman (Walad al-Amah)
Ruling on child of slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a child born to a slave woman and apply the conditions that determine whether the child is free or a slave.

Core Idea
A child of a slave woman follows the mother in status unless the father is her master – then the child is free.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' clarifies a key Hanafi rule: the child of a slave woman (amah) is not automatically free even if the father is free. The ruling hinges on who the father is and the mother's condition at the time of birth. We will unpack the main rule, its exceptions, and a subtle distinction about manumission by following vs. original manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and possible fathers
The act is the birth of a child to a slave woman. There are two possibilities for the father: her husband (who is not her master) or her master (mawla).
2
Apply the rule based on father's identity
If the father is the husband (not the master), the child is owned by the mother's master. If the father is the master, the child is free.
This is the core distinction.
3
Consider shared ownership
If the mother is owned by two or more persons, the child is shared according to their shares in the mother.
4
Analyze the effect of subsequent manumission
If the mother is manumitted, the child follows her in freedom only if at least six months elapsed between the manumission and the birth. Otherwise, the wala' (patronage) goes to the father's masters.
This timing condition prevents retroactive freedom.
5
Note exceptions and special cases
Two exceptions: (1) the child of a duped spouse (al-maghrouri) is free but compensation is paid; (2) if a slave marries his master's slave woman, the child is free because it is considered the master's child.
The commentary also clarifies that discussing manumission by following is not a repetition of earlier discussion of original manumission of the fetus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وولد الأمة من زوجها ملك لسيّدِها، وولدها من مولاها حرّ وإن كانت الأم مشتركة كان الولد مشتركاً على سهام الأم، وإن كانت مرقوقة ، فالولد المولود حال رقيتها يكون مرقوقاً ، وكذا يتبعها في العتق وفروعه : كالكتابة ، والتدبير، فعتق الولد بتبعيَّةِ الأُمِّ إنّما يكونُ إذا كان بين العتق والولادة ستة أشهر أو أكثر ، فحينئذ ينجر الولاء إلى موالي الأب، فعلم أنه لا تكرار . [قوله : مشتركة ؛ أي بين اثنين فأكثر، فالولد المولود من تلك الجارية يكون مشتركاً على قدر حصصهم في الأم.] [قوله : مرقوقة ؛ سواء كانت مملوكة أو لا، فإنّ بين الملك والرق عموماً وخصوصاً من وجه على ما مرّ سابقاً غير مرة، خلافاً لما ذكره الشارح له سابقاً من أنه لا يكون مرقوقاً إلا بأن يكون مملوكاً.] [قوله : في العتق ...الخ ؛ فإذا أعتق المولى الجارية عتق ولدها تبعاً لها، وكذا إذا دبرت صار مدبّراً، وكذا إذا كوتبت دخلَ في كتابتها، وهذا كله تبعاً لا أصالة.] [قوله : فعلم أنه لا تكرار ؛ دفع لما يرد على المصنف له أنه قد ذكر عتق الحمل بعتق الأم سابقاً ، ثم ذكر تبعية الولد للأم في الرق فهو تكرار، وحاصل الدفع أن الحكم السابق كان في عتق الحمل أصالة، وهذا في عتقه تبعاً فلا تكرار، وقد مر سابقاً وجه الفرق بينهما.] [قوله : ملك لسيدها ؛ لما مرّ من أنّ الولد يتبع الأم في الرق والملك، فلا يكون حراً، وإن كان أبوه حرّاً، ويستثنى منه ولد المغرور ؛ فإنّه حرّ بالقيمة، كان يتزوج الحر امرأة على أنها حرّة ، فإذا هي قنة، فأولاده منها أحراراً بالقيمة، وقد يكون الولد حراً من رقيقين بلا تحرير ، كأن نكح عبد أمة أبيه فولده حرّ ؛ لأنه ولد ولد المولى. كذا في «الظهيرية».] [قوله : حرّ ؛ لأنه مخلوق من مائه فيعتق عليه. كذا في «الهداية»]
And the child of a slave woman from her husband is the property of her master, and her child from her master is free. If the mother is shared (between two or more), the child is shared according to the shares in the mother. If she is a slave (marquqa), then the child born while she is a slave is also a slave. Similarly, the child follows her in manumission and its derivatives, such as kitaba (writing a contract of manumission) and tadbir (posthumous manumission). The child's manumission through following the mother only occurs if there are six months or more between the manumission and the birth; then the wala' (patronage) goes to the master of the father. So it is understood that there is no repetition. [His statement: 'shared' – meaning between two or more, so the child born from that slave woman is shared according to their shares in the mother.] [His statement: 'slave' – whether she is owned or not, because between ownership and slavery there is a general-specific relationship as previously mentioned many times, contrary to what the commentator earlier stated that she is not a slave unless she is owned.] [His statement: 'in manumission etc.' – when the master manumits the slave woman, her child is manumitted following her, and similarly if she is made mudabbara, he becomes mudabbar, and if she is given a kitaba, he enters into her kitaba. Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage from the commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' expands on the rulings related to the child of a slave woman (umm walad). It is a ruling_statement that explains how the child's status (free or slave) depends on the father and the mother's condition. The main ruling: if a slave woman has a child from her husband (who is not her master), the child is owned by her master. If the father is her master (mawla), the child is free. If the mother is owned jointly, the child is owned jointly according to the shares in the mother. The child follows the mother in her status of slavery or freedom. Importantly, if the mother is manumitted, the child is also manumitted provided there is at least six months between the manumission and the birth; otherwise, the wala' goes to the father's patrons. The commentary addresses potential repetition: earlier the text discussed manumission of the fetus as an original act, while here it discusses manumission by following, so no repetition. An exception is the case of al-maghrouri (a duped spouse), where the child is free but compensation is paid. Another scenario: if a slave marries his master's slave woman, the child is free because it is considered the child of the master. The commentary relies on Al-Zahiriya and Al-Hidaya as sources.

Key Terms
ولد الأمة (walad al-amah): The child of a slave woman; its legal status is determined by paternity and mother's condition as per Hanafi fiqh.
مرقوقة (marqūqah): A female slave in a state of slavery; may or may not be owned (ownership and slavery are distinct).
المغرور (al-maghrou): A person who marries under a false belief about the spouse's free status, leading to children being free with compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave woman (amah) has a child from her husband who is not her master, what is the child's status?
A) The child is free because the father is free.
B) The child is owned by the master of the mother.
C) The child is a slave owned jointly by both parents' masters.
D) The child is free but must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
The child of a slave woman is owned by her master unless the father is the master himself, in which case the child is free.

Partial Manumission: Imam Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Presents Hanafi ruling with intra-school dispute and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partial manumission, explain the intra-school dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the hadith evidence supporting Abu Hanifa's position.

Core Idea
Partial manumission is valid and irreversible; the slave earns the remainder but never reverts to slavery.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on freeing only part of a slave. While Imam Abu Hanifa holds that partial manumission is valid and the slave must work to pay the remaining value, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that the entire slave becomes free immediately. The commentator clarifies the supporting evidence and the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa
Identify that according to Abu Hanifa, freeing part of one's slave is valid (sahih). The slave becomes partially free and must work (sāʿā) to earn the remaining value of his freedom. This is the established position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The master must clarify if the freed portion is ambiguous.
2
Identify the opposing view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the entire slave is freed immediately upon the master's declaration. Their reasoning is not fully detailed here but likely stems from the principle of avoiding partial slavery.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
The commentator cites a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave... otherwise he has freed what he freed.' This explicitly permits partial manumission, supporting Abu Hanifa.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear.
4
Understand the distinction from a mukatab
A partially freed slave is like a mukatab (slave under contract) in many rulings (cannot be sold, does not inherit, etc.). However, if the slave fails to pay, the mukatab reverts to slavery while the partially freed slave does not, because manumission has already taken effect.
This distinction reinforces the irrevocability of partial manumission.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
Later scholars (e.g., author of al-Jami' al-Mudmarat) confirm that the correct position is Abu Hanifa's. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the slave works to pay; under Sahibayn the slave is fully free immediately.
The hadith is the primary basis for tarjih.

باب عتق البعض (وإذا أعتق بعض عبده صح، وسعى فيما بقي، وهو كالمكاتب بلا رد إلى الرّق لو عجز، وقالا : عتق كله) [قوله : بعض عبده ؛ سواء كان البعض معيناً كالنصف والربع، أو مبهماً كجزء منك حراً، وشيء منك حرّ، ويلزم المولى حينئذ بيانه. كذا في «الخانية». ولو قال بعض العبد من دون إضافة لكان أولى ؛ ليشمل إعتاق أحد الشركاء في عبد سهمه فيه ، فإنّ ظاهر قوله : «بعض عبده»، يوجب اختصاص الحكم ببعض عبده المملوك له خاصة، وإنّما اختار هذه العبارة لكون مقصوده بيان حكم إعتاق الشريكِ على حدة على ما سيأتي.] [قوله : وسعى ؛ أي سعى العبد الذي أعتق بعضه لمولاه في قيمة بقيته التي لم تعتق، وصورة الاستسعاء أن يؤاجره المولى ويأخذ قيمة ما بقي من أجره.] [قوله : كالمكاتب ؛ في أنه لا يباعُ ولا يرث ولا يورث، ولا يتزوج، ولا تقبلُ شهادته، ويصير أحق بمكاسبه ؛ وذلك لأنه تعلق خلاص كله بأداء مال، كما في المكاتب. ويفترق عنه في أن المكاتب إذا عجز عن أداء بدل الكتابة يصير رقيقاً كما كان ، ولا كذلك معتق البعض ؛ فإنه لو عجز عن أداء قيمة الباقي لا يصير رقيقاً كما كان ؛ لوجود الإعتاق فيه من المولى دون المكاتب.] [قوله : وقالا ؛ ذكر صاحب «الجامع المضمرات» وغيره : إن الصحيح في هذا الباب قول الإمام ، ويويده حديث : «مَن أعتق شركاً له في عبده كان له مال يبلغ ثمن العبد قوّم عليه قيمة عدل، فأعطى شركاءه حصصهم، وعتق عليه العبد، وإلا فقد عتق منه ما أعتق) ، أخرجته الأئمة السنّة، فإنه يدلُّ صريحاً على تصوّر عتق البعض دون الكل.]
Chapter on Partial Manumission (If someone frees part of his slave, it is valid, and the slave works to pay for what remains, and he is like a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) with no returning to slavery if he is unable. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the whole slave is freed.) [His statement: 'part of his slave' – whether the part is specified, like half or quarter, or ambiguous, like 'a part of you is free' or 'something of you is free'. Then the master must clarify. So in al-Khaniya. And if he said 'some of the slave' without specification, it would be better to include the freeing of one partner's share in a slave; for the apparent meaning of 'part of his slave' restricts the ruling to part of his own slave specifically. He chose this expression because his purpose is to state the ruling for the partner's manumission separately, as will come.] [His statement: 'works to pay' – meaning the slave who has been partially freed works for his master to pay the value of the remaining part that was not freed. The manner of istis'a' is that the master hires him out and takes the value of what remains from his wages.] [His statement: 'like a mukatab' – in that he cannot be sold, does not inherit, is not inherited, cannot marry, his testimony is not accepted, and he becomes entitled to his own earnings; because his complete freedom is tied to paying a sum, as in the case of a mukatab. But it differs from the mukatab in that if the mukateb is unable to pay the kitaba amount, he becomes a slave again as before, but not so for the one partially freed; for if he is unable to pay the value of the remaining part, he does not become a slave again as before, because the manumission has occurred from the master, unlike the mukatab.] [His statement: 'and they said' – the author of al-Jami' al-Mudmarat and others said that the correct view in this chapter is the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), supported by the hadith: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave and has enough wealth to reach the full price of the slave, he shall be evaluated with a fair value, and give his partners their shares, and the slave is freed. Otherwise, he has freed what he freed.' It is reported by the imams of the Sunnah, and it explicitly indicates the possibility of freeing part without the whole.]
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the chapter of partial manumission (bāb ʿitq al-baʿḍ). It first presents the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: if a master frees part of his slave, the manumission is valid, and the slave must work (sāʿā) to pay the remaining value of his freedom. The slave's status is similar to that of a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission), but with a key difference: if a mukatab fails to pay, he reverts to slavery, whereas the partially freed slave does not revert because the manumission is already effective from the master. In contrast, the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, referred to as 'qālā') hold that the entire slave is freed (i.e., the partial manumission triggers full manumission). The commentary then explains that the correct position according to most later scholars is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, supported by a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim which clearly allows partial manumission. The detailed commentary clarifies that 'some of his slave' can be specified (like half) or ambiguous, and the master must clarify. The istis'ā' process is described as the master hiring out the slave to earn the remaining value. The comparison with mukatab highlights that the partially freed slave has more rights because the manumission has already commenced.

Key Terms
عتق البعض (ʿitq al-baʿḍ): Manumission of a part of a slave; the chapter's subject.
سعى (sāʿā): The slave works to earn money to pay the remaining value of his freedom.
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave under a contract of manumission (kitaba) who pays installments to earn freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens if a master frees half of his slave and the slave cannot earn the remaining value?
A) The slave becomes fully free because the master intended half.
B) The slave remains partially free and cannot be sold back into slavery.
C) The slave reverts to full slavery.
D) The master must free the remaining half.

Key Takeaway
Partial manumission is valid; the slave works to pay the remainder and never reverts to slavery upon inability.

Partial Manumission: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute over the legal effect of partial manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's views on partial manumission and identify the relied-upon position based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Partial manumission is valid, but only the freed part becomes free; the slave must earn the remaining value.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of freeing a part of a slave. While all agree that the act of partial manumission is valid, they differ on whether it frees only the stated part or the entire slave. This disagreement stems from a deeper conceptual difference: is manumission removal of ownership (divisible) or removal of slavery (indivisible)? We will explore the evidence and determine the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
First, recognize that the act is manumitting a part (ba'd) of one's slave. Abu Hanifa holds that only the specified part becomes free, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the entire slave becomes free.
The disagreement is not about the validity of the act itself.
2
Understand istis'a' and the mukatab analogy
The slave must earn (istis'a') the value of the unfreed portion for the master. He is compared to a mukatab (slave under contract) in most aspects except that he does not revert to slavery if unable to pay.
This shows the practical consequence of Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith 'Whoever frees a share he has in a slave... otherwise what he freed becomes free' is the key proof for Abu Hanifa. It explicitly validates partial manumission.
The hadith is authentic (Sahih al-Bukhari, Muslim).
4
Examine the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn argue that manumission (i'taq) is the removal of slavery, which is indivisible. Therefore, freeing part implies freeing the whole. They analogize to breaking a whole object.
Their reasoning is aqli (rational) based on the nature of freedom.
5
Conclude with tarjih
The author of al-Jami' al-Mudmarat and others state that the correct position is Abu Hanifa's due to the explicit hadith. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The conceptual key: Abu Hanifa defines i'taq as removal of ownership (divisible), while the Sahibayn define it as removal of slavery (indivisible).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب عتق البعض
وإذا أعتق بعض عبده صح، وسعى فيما بقي، وهو كالمكاتب بلا رد إلى الرّق لو عجز، وقالا : عتق كله
قوله: بعض عبده؛ سواء كان البعض معيناً كالنصف والربع، أو مبهماً كجزء منك حراً، وشيء منك حرّ، ويلزم المولى حينئذ بيانه. كذا في «الخانية». ولو قال بعض العبد من دون إضافة لكان أولى؛ ليشمل إعتاق أحد الشركاء في عبد سهمه فيه، فإنّ ظاهر قوله: «بعض عبده»، يوجب اختصاص الحكم ببعض عبده المملوك له خاصة، وإنّما اختار هذه العبارة لكون مقصوده بيان حكم إعتاق الشريكِ على حدة على ما سيأتي.
قوله: وسعى؛ أي سعى العبد الذي أعتق بعضه لمولاه في قيمة بقيته التي لم تعتق، وصورة الاستسعاء أن يؤاجره المولى ويأخذ قيمة ما بقي من أجره.
قوله: كالمكاتب؛ في أنه لا يباعُ ولا يرث ولا يورث، ولا يتزوج، ولا تقبلُ شهادته، ويصير أحق بمكاسبه؛ وذلك لأنه تعلق خلاص كله بأداء مال، كما في المكاتب. ويفترق عنه في أن المكاتب إذا عجز عن أداء بدل الكتابة يصير رقيقاً كما كان، ولا كذلك معتق البعض؛ فإنه لو عجز عن أداء قيمة الباقي لا يصير رقيقاً كما كان؛ لوجود الإعتاق فيه من المولى دون المكاتب.
قوله: وقالا؛ ذكر صاحب «الجامع المضمرات» وغيره: إن الصحيح في هذا الباب قول الإمام، ويؤيده حديث: «من أعتق شركاً له في عبده كان له مال يبلغ ثمن العبد قوّم عليه قيمة عدل، فأعطى شركاءه حصصهم، وعتق عليه العبد، وإلا فقد عتق منه ما أعتق»، أخرجته الأئمة السنّة، فإنه يدلُّ صريحاً على تصوّر عتق البعض دون الكل. هذا بناءً على أن العتق لا يتجزأ بالاتفاق، فكذا الإعتاق عندهما؛ لأنه إثباتُ العتق، كالكسر مع الانكسار فيلزم من عدم تجزَةِ اللازم، وهو العتق، عدم تجزؤ ملزومه، وهو الاعتاق، لكن أبا حنيفة له يقول: الاعتاق إزالة الملك؛ لأنَّه ليس للمالك إلا إزالة حقه، وهو الملك.
قوله: لا يتجزأ بالاتفاق؛ قال الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في شرح الكنز: «أصله: إنّ الإعتاق يوجب زوال الملك عنده، وهو متجزئ، وعندهما يوجب زوال الرق وهو غير متجزئ، وأما نفس الإعتاق أو العتق فلا يتجزأ بالإجماع؛ لأن ذات الفعل وهو العلة، وحكمه وهو نزول الحرية فيه لا يتصوّر فيه التجزؤ، وكذا الرق لا يتجزا بالإجماع؛ لأنه ضعف حكمي، والحريّة قوّة حكميّة فلا يتصور إجتماعها في شخص واحد. فإذا ثبت هذا، فأبو حنيفة اعتبر جانب الرق فجعل كله رقيقاً على ما كان، وقد زال ملكه عن البعض الذي أعتقه، وهما اعتبرا جانب الحرية، فصار كله حراً». انتهى
وفي «العناية» نقلاً عن «الميزان»: «المعني من قولنا: الإعتاق يتجزأ ليس هو أن ذات القول تتجزأ أو حكمه يتجزا؛ لأنه محال، بل معنى ذلك أن المحل في قبول حكم الإعتاق يتجزأ، فيتصوّر ثبوته في النصف دون النصف، وحاصل الخلافِ راجع إلى أن إعتاق النصف هل يوجب زوال الرقّ عن المحلّ كلّه، فعنده لا يوجب، بل يبقى الكل رقيقاً، ولكن زالَ الملك بقدره، وعندهما يوجب زوال الرق عن الكل». انتهى
Chapter: Manumission of a Part
And if he frees a part of his slave, it is valid, and he (the slave) shall earn for what remains, and he is like a mukatab without return to slavery if he is incapable. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the whole becomes free.
His saying: "a part of his slave" — whether the part is specified like half or quarter, or ambiguous like 'a part of you is free' or 'something of you is free', and then the master is obliged to clarify. So in al-Khaniyya. And if he said 'a part of the slave' without addition, it would be better to include the manumission of one of the partners in a slave of his share, for the apparent meaning of his saying 'a part of his slave' requires restricting the ruling to a part of his own slave. He chose this expression because his aim is to explain the ruling of a partner's manumission separately, as will come.
His saying: "and he shall earn" — i.e., the slave whose part is freed shall earn for his master the value of the remaining part that was not freed. The form of istis'a' is that the master hires him out and takes the value of what remains from his wages.
His saying: "like a mukatab" — in that he cannot be sold, nor inherits, nor is inherited from, nor marries, nor is his testimony accepted, and he becomes more entitled to his earnings. This is because his complete deliverance is attached to payment of money, as in the mukatab. And it differs in that the mukatab, if unable to pay the substitute of kitaba, becomes a slave as before, but not the one with partial manumission; for if he is unable to pay the value of the remainder, he does not become a slave as before, due to the existence of manumission from the master, unlike the mukatab.
His saying: "and the two said" — the author of al-Jami' al-Mudmarat and others said: The correct in this chapter is the saying of al-Imam (Abu Hanifa), and it is supported by the hadith: "Whoever frees a share he has in a slave and has money that reaches the price of the slave, he shall be valued with a just value, gives the partners their shares, and the slave becomes free on him; otherwise, what he freed becomes free." Recorded by the imams of the Sunnah. It explicitly indicates the possibility of manumission of a part without the whole. This is based on the fact that manumission (al-'itq) is not divisible by consensus. So also manumission (al-i'taq) according to them (the two), because it is the establishment of manumission, like breaking with breakage, so from the impossibility of division of the necessary (manumission), the impossibility of division of its prerequisite (i'taq) follows. But Abu Hanifa says: manumission (i'taq) is removal of ownership, because the owner has only the removal of his right, which is ownership.
His saying: "not divisible by consensus" — al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz said: "Its origin: i'taq necessitates removal of ownership according to him (Abu Hanifa), and it is divisible; according to them (the two) it necessitates removal of slavery, which is not divisible. As for i'taq itself or 'itq itself, it is not divisible by consensus, because the essence of the act which is the cause, and its ruling which is the descent of freedom in it, cannot be divided. Likewise, slavery is not divisible by consensus, because it is a legal weakness, and freedom is a legal strength, so their combination in one person cannot be imagined. So when this is established, Abu Hanifa considered the aspect of slavery and made the whole a slave as before, but his ownership has ceased over the part he freed; and the two considered the aspect of freedom, so the whole became free." End.
And in al-'Inaya quoting from al-Mizan: "The meaning of our saying 'i'taq is divisible' is not that the essence of the statement is divisible or its ruling is divisible, because that is impossible. Rather, the meaning is that the locus (al-mahall) in accepting the ruling of i'taq is divisible, so its establishment in half without the other half is conceivable. And the essence of the dispute returns to whether the manumission of half necessitates removal of slavery from the entire locus. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it does not necessitate, but the whole remains a slave, but ownership has ceased by its extent. According to them (the two), it necessitates removal of slavery from the whole." End.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of manumitting a part of one's slave. The text begins by stating the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa: if a master frees a part of his slave, the manumission is valid only for that part, and the slave must earn (through istis'a') to pay for the remaining value. The slave is like a mukatab in that he cannot be sold, inherits, etc., but differs in that he does not revert to slavery if unable to pay. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the entire slave becomes free. The commentary then explains that the disagreement is based on whether the act of manumission (i'taq) is removal of ownership (which is divisible) or removal of slavery (which is indivisible). Abu Hanifa considers i'taq as removing ownership, so it can be partial. The Sahibayn consider it as removing slavery, which cannot be partial, so partial manumission entails full freedom. The hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) about freeing a share in a jointly owned slave is cited to support Abu Hanifa's view, as it explicitly mentions partial manumission. The commentator also notes that the correct position in this chapter is that of Abu Hanifa. The deeper principle is that while the status of freedom or slavery is indivisible (hence 'itq/raqq are not divisible), the legal act of i'taq can be considered removable of ownership, which is divisible. Thus, according to Abu Hanifa, the slave remains a slave but the master's ownership over the freed part ceases, and the slave must earn to compensate.

Key Terms
عتق البعض (ʿitq al-baʿḍ): Manumission of a part of a slave, whether specified or ambiguous, leading to partial freedom.
استسعاء (istisʿāʾ): The slave's earning (through hiring out) to pay the value of the unfreed portion to the master.
مكاتب (mukātib): A slave who has contracted with his master to earn and pay for his freedom. Here, the partially freed slave is compared to him in legal status but differs in that he does not revert to slavery if unable to pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding partial manumission?
A) Whether the slave can be sold after partial manumission
B) Whether manumission removes ownership or slavery
C) Whether the slave must pay for his freedom
D) Whether the manumission contract is valid

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that partial manumission frees only the specified part, supported by explicit hadith.

Ruling on a Partner Freeing His Share of a Jointly Owned Slave
Explains Hanafi ruling with proof on partial emancipation of jointly owned slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a co-owner frees his share of a joint slave, explain the proof based on divisible ownership, and identify the three options available to the other co-owner.

Core Idea
Freeing a share does not free the whole slave; ownership's divisibility governs partial emancipation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a core Hanafi ruling on partial emancipation. Many students mistakenly assume that freeing a portion of a jointly owned slave frees the entire slave. Here, Al-Marghinani (via the commentator) explains why this is not so, using qiyas on divisible transactions like sale and gift. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi approach to ownership and its removal, and introduces important concepts like istis'a' and tadmeen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Immediate Ruling
The act is that one co-owner frees his share of a jointly owned slave. The immediate ruling: the slave does not become fully free; only the share of the freeing partner is emancipated.
Contrast with the common misconception that partial emancipation frees the entire slave.
2
Examine the Proof from Divisible Ownership
The proof is that ownership is divisible (al-milk mutajazzi'). Emancipation is the removal of ownership. Since removal corresponds to what is owned, freeing only a share removes only that share's ownership.
The passage compares to sale and gift: selling a half-share transfers only that half.
3
Analyze the Qiyas of Sale and Gift
The commentator explicitly analogizes to transactions: just as selling or gifting a portion of a slave transfers ownership of that portion only, emancipation (being a disposal of ownership) likewise affects only the portion owned by the actor.
This is qiyas jaliy: the illa is the divisibility of ownership.
4
List the Options of the Other Partner
The other co-owner has three options: (1) free his own share immediately or conditionally, (2) demand the slave to earn (istis'a') to pay the value of his share, or (3) demand compensation (tadmeen) from the freeing partner if that partner is wealthy.
If the freeing partner is poor, only options (1) and (2) are available.
5
Consider Conditions and Consequences
The other partner must be legally capable (adult, sane). If incapable, we wait. Wala' (clientage) is shared between both partners if the other chooses to free or demand istis'a'. If tadmeen is taken, the freeing partner is considered the sole liberator for wala' purposes.
Conditions like wealth of the freeing partner are assessed at the time of emancipation.

Source Text
